de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or too great evacuation, or from seeming of cold matter spread out, no one of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the sick person be freed of pills made from fetid things or other semblances, and one makes it on their back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 cauters or more according to virtue and quantity that the sick person can bear; and the cauter is made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see, make 3 cauters or 4 at the middle-cautery "clavile" according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have tight limbs when they awaken, and pain; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and on the appearance that comes above the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it heal, then cauterize at the cautery of the back according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If you apply a crimson cautery to each part of the spine equally. And if you see that it is necessary to cauterize around the spine with the red-hot cautery, do two or three lines so that the points are close to one another. Then cure the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and be sure not to bring a cautery near a swelling of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by a swelling that spreads to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which they call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, so it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and be the cauteries olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you take the point of the foot, then make a cautery all over the point that we call "point". And if the pains come up to the knee and at other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cautery on each kneecap three or four cauteries from each part, in all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do it, but hold your hand out no longer than until the flesh of the wound is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the sides or down to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good management with the patient and administer medicines. For if you do good management and bleed him, he will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an obstruction comes in the intestines, and the bowels descend to the groin and it is new, so it is necessary that when you see it needs to be cured, do not cut into him that day; and let him use things which loosen the belly, so that the feces descend from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relaxed, and remove them to your right, and sign with a mark under the obstruction above the bone of the elbow, and in all a sign which is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which it is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and he has passed stools. Then remove the bowels to their place; and have the servant hold his hand so that they do not return behind; and take good care of the legs of the patient, and put a cushion underneath him and a sergeant on the thighs, and another on the chest which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your might, and your right hand and your left hand until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again once more until you feel the bone; and take heed carefully so that the bowels do not spill when you make the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that through this the patient does not die, or suffer another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their measure, and those of old people also as large as their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the inflammation is removed; then cure him with other ointments until he is healed, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed. And it is necessary that his stitches be left for a long time, so that the bowels do not spill when he will go to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .xl. days, when he wants to get up, instruct him with a good bandage and have him rest for .xl. more days; and give him good rest, so that he does not tire himself out or over-replenish himself with drink and food, and do not make him breathe too loudly; and when he follows this instruction, he will be entirely cured. And I will say the treatment of cauterizing in its chapter after this.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come into other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make him have one cauterization of the cauterizer according to its quantity, and let it be red with the third part of the gall; after which cure him in accordance with what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that we should cauterize at the cauterizer to three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first sign is to show the lead of the incision and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another below it, and with your hand fill in the whole cauterizer with clay. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more uncertain.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, whether from a fall or a cut, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cauterizer called "poins", and let the cauterizations be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its virtues and its location in terms of twisting and pain. If he is cured from the first cauterization, it's good; if not, repeat another cauterization on top of that, because custom says that it should change in the member that is nearest to it, so you should make the cauterizations as long as the sick person remains uncured.
de meselerie	of wound healing (or surgery)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The physician is aided sometimes by cautery with great help, and the same sickness that comes from putrefaction of bad blood and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the sickness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not remain or disappear, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one between the eyebrows, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the occipital bone; and leave your hand so that the cauteries reach just to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize on the nose according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread throughout; and it is manifestly being wasted, it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head which we have said, and one cautery on the nape, and two cauteres on the spine of the neck, and five cauteres on the spine of the back, and one large one on the scrotum and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the thighs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the pits of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the spine, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cautery I make, the more aid and progress it brings; and know that the sick person does not feel pain during the cautery, just as the healthy ones do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And it's necessary that the cauteries are large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
de enfleure	From a swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When a swelling comes in any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it's not healed, then make cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterie be a small one entering into the depth of the skin; then cure it with ointments until it's healed. And sometimes make cautery at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus remove the swelling; and however, no one intervenes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has grown old, and medical remedies are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery that is deep, according to the size of the skin, until the ulcer is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of wheat and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of goose and blood of crane, each one in equal part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at high place until it's healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre comes at the beginning, and you see it to stop, if you apply fire to the cautery which seems like a circle, around it all over the chancre. And nevertheless wise men say that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, for I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen some time ago; and more proper thing is that it be cauterized around, at the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of a swelling which cannot perish (die)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease which is called "adubelati", and it takes too long to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has pus in his veins, or because of the weather; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries that pierce; after leaving him thus. For it will hasten to perish.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery until its form is like this: (note: there seems to be a blank line or omission in the original text at this point)
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced to the core, and be such the cautery that the patient feels it everywhere in such a way that the current of the rotting is alleviated. Then cure him as long as he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron (presumably referring to a surgical procedure using cautery)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease which is called "corrodens", and it's nothing but a gangrene of the member, for it eats up the members just like fire does to dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where a cautery with fire can be applied, then heat the cauterizers, very small and very large, according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; after that cauterize all around until you are able to remove all the corruption, and let nothing remain of it, except for removing all that which is corrupted. And then leave it for three days, and put on the places cauterized oil so that they can broil with it until the burnings of fire are removed, and all the corruption. After that apply an ointment to heal wounds of flesh. If you see after three days that healthy flesh has grown, it's good; and if not, then reapply the cautery on what remains from the places corrupted. And this gangrene has been cured sometimes with medicinal poultice instead of cautery with fire; but nonetheless cautery with fire is of greater help, and I have already said in a division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the splinters that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	often times it happens that the feet, in winter, fall ill with a sickness called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large, hardened thing that wounds the foot. And the sores of this disease are, according to us, in two ways: cauterization by fire, and cauterization by hot water.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted by force of the body, and many times occurs in hands and feet, then you must apply a cautery with hot water; and thus: take a lead or iron tube, or a quill made from calamus, and place on the nail and the surrounding flesh, that is to say the pores and warts; and place the tube so that it surrounds everything, then put in a small amount of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and you can find the deep penetration of hot water just to the root; and allow the patient to endure the burning of hot water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will pull out all its roots. Thus make another one after another, until you have extracted all those that are on the body, then cure them with ointments that engender flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold or fever quartan or another thing, then it is necessary that you make 4 cauterizations or 5 on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped part; he will stop trembling, and hasten to health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	The cure for boils or pustules (puans in Old French). Here is a continuation of the text:
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appear on the body boils, or suppurating pustules, which come from large corrupt matter. So it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a fine cautery made of mistletoe wood, whose tip has been grasped by fire, or a long aristolochia root, or a lentil-shaped cautery. And sometimes when you cauterize them at first when they appear in this way, and they cannot grow any further ahead, but the superfluous matter from which they come is broken down and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after blood evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there occur great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut to the wound that comes first, or to the incision of the apostema, or to the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger over the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the bleeding ceases under your finger, and no more blood flows; then take several small and large olive oil cauteries as many as are needed, heat them up so that they are all red; then grasp one, either a large or small one according to the wound and its location where the artery runs, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth when you lift your finger off the vein, and the cautery is spent, then take another one quickly from among those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this until the bleeding is stopped. Be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it can hardly be stopped on its own when the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not already tied off, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medications that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be closed and tightened properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will remind them of the danger of tightly tying a ligature or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if they do not know what they are doing.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a surgeon or physician present, then he should put his index finger over the wound of the vein just as we said, and press hard until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move his finger, but rather wet it with cold water often until it is very cold so that the bleeding is frozen and thickened and stopped; and he should make inquiries ahead of time for things that will be needed from cauteries and medications.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with hot medicine, and the instruments and causes and reasons and forms of cauterizations; and I placed that chapter at the beginning just up to a point, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that you find what you want more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and because of that it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there are many times an evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and making an incision above a pustule, and caring for wounds, and extracting splinters, and making an incision on the bone, and similar things; or else there is doubt and fear, and the patient comes to more harm.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you not undertake foolishness. For many kinds of people come to be cured. Some come with such a disease that they die easily because of the suddenness of their illness, and from the greatness of their suffering; and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who will give you their reason, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful. You should not consent to see those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely towards those of whom you are certain and from whom you can gain praise; and use prognosis and indication in treating your patients for the sake of their salvation; and that will help you achieve good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe with the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. (This is a final blessing, typical in medieval texts.)
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in sections, as I was explaining by chapters, according to what is written before the chapter on cauterizations, which I explained from beginning to end for you, so that you would find it easier to understand the things of which you will need. (This is a conclusion and final statement, wrapping up the explanation of the chapter.)
dou chief plein d’aigue	A vessel full of water. (This appears to be a simple phrase or description, possibly referring back to some earlier context in the text where the use of a vessel was mentioned.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the cord compresses too strongly the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a reason that is unknown. (This phrase appears to be a medical explanation or warning about a possible cause of a specific illness.)
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and with all that I've seen the death rate has been high; and because of this it seems to me that it's not worth the effort to treat them. (This phrase appears to be a conclusion drawn by the author based on their experience and observations.)
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose eyes were full of water, and the head was swelling every day so much that it could no longer be sustained; and he was so weak that he seemed to be dead, and this weakness is assembled under the bone above the eye socket, between the skull and the bone; and the operation is like this: if the weakness is between the skull and the bone, and the tumors are small, you make an incision in the head of a width of two fingers, as long as the weakness runs; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is under the bone, and you see signs that the corners of the head are open on each side, and when you press it with your hand from the inside, it springs up high, and it does not return to its original shape: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove the swelling completely. Afterwards, close the wounds with bandages and powders, and put wine and oil on them, and leave it in that state until the fifth day; then untie it, and treat the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the head to drain equally, and give the patient dry food, such as soup of the swelling itself, until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to make the incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess and the drainage are assembled; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes at the back, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the abscess opens and the drainage is collected, and make the incision as far as you can, but be careful not to cut the artery; and if you see a lot of bleeding, let it flow, so that the patient may die from blood loss and the evacuation of the swelling.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease that is called "catarre" (likely referring to an abscess or tumor in the groin or armpit) and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last cure is to cauterize with what will close the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	So, when you see that the two arteries are covered, it is necessary for the patient to raise their head; after which scrape the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear. Then take the patient's collar and tie them up with all sorts of clothes; then look where the vein bites, and the place on one side and the other are behind the ears, and the places are swollen; then mark the places to cut, then cut both with an acursed spatula of two parts, so that the flesh comes down just to the bone, and let it be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see fit, insert the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting also as two blades through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood sprays upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not bleed enough, you should measure three fingers' breadth above it, then cut down to the bone; and what needs to be taken out is six cells [or ounces], and maybe a little more or less, according to how much the patient can bear, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if pus remains on top of the bone, cut off the dead tissue that comes, then clean the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient headache comes, and sharp catarrh, by reason of the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old severe fever and similar things, and all manner of medical treatments help him not, then we cut out the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the sick person makes themselves go bald on their temples, and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, for it beats well and pushes out quite a lot in some men who are too cold; and if it is visible, then the sick person ties their own hair with some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and heats up the area with hot water until the artery shows manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then peel the thin skin slightly until you come to the artery, then grab it at the top with forceps and separate it well from the threads that are under each part; and if the artery is fine, turn it into a point on the hook of the knife, then cut off that part according to the length of two fingers. For if it is not cut, the blood will not drain out completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And remove the blood from two to three cells, and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two knots with a strong double thread of silk, so that no infection comes before the wound closes and bleeding stops; then cut off the excess that is between the two knots at the same hour, and afterwards, if you see fit, cauterize it with a cauterizing knife until the bone, as long as the fingers are cut off. This is the main work, if the sick person has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is helpful to finish the wounds: for that reason it is of greater help to the wounds.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made bandages; and when you untie them, be careful to use dry medicines that make flesh grow, and bandages, until they are healed; and if there is bleeding from the artery as much as you work, hasten to cauterize by fire, or fill the place with vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the bleeding is stopped; and if you do not have this present, put on the place your thumb so long as the bleeding is congealed, and bind the place with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be careful as it is necessary; and what is more fragile and lighter in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with a trenching cautery cutting to two parts, but the trenching should be well spread so as to keep the heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two blades one inch of space, and then when you mark to enclose the two places, and you lay the hot iron on them so that it comes up just to the bone, and cut the vein in two pieces; and be separated between the two cuts because they are not completely joined by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	It seems you've started a new sentence.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are on the root of the eye's forehead, and it does not benefit from the care of medicine made there, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel the front ambulation as if with tremors; and since they are swollen and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids are fallen, and are scalded the eyelids, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they used to call it the "cure of contusion", and it is that you make the hairs on the forehead of the patient who has this disease fall out, then you make three incisions on the forehead equally in length; and one of the incisions is as long as two fingers from below upwards, and the other two are each one finger away from the eyelids above, and take care to avoid cutting the arteries that are at the sides above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the mandibles, and let each wound be the length of three fingers across the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a piece of sponge and moistened it with cloth to stop the bleeding, then insert the sponge into the wound up to two parts of its depth, which is the shape:

The instructions are to:
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument in the first cut, which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side not sharp, this is its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the sharp edge towards the cut meat to the knife, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the first incision. And cut off all the vessels that descend from the head to themselves as much as the incision is continuous up to where it opens at the cut, and then do the other half in the first incision up to the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the collected blood; then put a piece of old cotton cloth in each incision, and put on moistened cloths with wine and oil and ashes, and take care that there are no post-emerges; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply great plantain paste, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The bond of their bones.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When they come with a common catarrh, and you see their eyes tight and small, and weakening the sight, and the papers burned; and the hair is falling out, and the head is deeply in pain, and the patient is sniveling; then know from these signs that those materials and the catarrh do not come but from many veins, and the mother womb cure that it is, this is.

Start from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that are in the temples that move at mealtime. When the bone is uncovered, squeeze out all the blood onto a sponge, and then wipe between the two lips of the incision with old cotton, and apply linen bandages. Then tie moistened cloths with wine and oil on top, and take care to prevent hot post-emerges; when it's removed, it's necessary that you rub the bone until pus begins to appear, then cure with purgatives that make flesh come out.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of gallnut paste, and make a poultice with them; and administer it in these wounds to discharge pus everywhere. (Note: Gallnuts are a type of plant material that has been used historically for medicinal purposes, including as an antiseptic and anti-inflammatory agent.)
de l’estoupement des oreilles	De l'estoupement des oreilles (French for "of the stopping up of the ears")...
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: or stones, or beasts, or mine stones or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas, lentils; or flowing things such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear a stone or another kind of thing that does not belong to the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, have it distill some violet oil or sesame oil, then perform extraction; and make the patient sneeze with condiments, and stop their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and elevate the ear above. Many times this remedy works; and if it does not work, have them extract the stone with subtle pincers, whose form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with pincers, that's good; if not, have them extract the stone with a subtle awl of small doublet; and if it doesn't come out in this way, make a chain of lead and put the end of the chain or the hole in the ear very tightly closed, and stop what is around the chain with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then press it firmly forward, for many times comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glue from which birds take hold, and put into a tool that is sharp enough to do this, and put some cotton around it; then press the glue on top of the stone or whatever it is, and press it forward.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stoppage of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien. Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So that which comes deep, if one cannot see it, is from severe inflammation in several dispositions, and for the one that one can see, you should put the ear of the sick person in the sun; and look inside: if you see a visible swelling, then the work has all this thickness of which I am speaking, namely the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee. Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the operation is to be done right through the ear, take a subtle, light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the ear. If you feel the operation from which the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce lightly, but make sure that you do not harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a plug according to the size of the hole, and moisten with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or you take a plug and moisten it in red rose water, and powder over vitriol broth; and if you see that the ear is swollen, then you must remove the plug and put another wetted plug made of rosset oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure him until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the bleeding does not stop, then plunge a sponge and wring it out in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the bleeding which are among the treatments of distillations.

de la gresle	Of hail.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char. de la graisse des eulz	It appears to be a medical text written in Old French.

des poilz des papieres	It seems like we've taken a turn from the medicinal instructions!
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz. Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if the patient needs it, cut off a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened. Then bring together the two lips with a stitch of a needle on one thread of fine wool, and dry up the blood, and make the superfluous threads stick to both earrings for anything that sticks, if you see fit; and if not, do not worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads until three or four days. Then cure the wound without stitches with dry and constraining things, because the paper revives at the solidity of the wound and its assembly, but the stitches are weak (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.

Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of cracks is in this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and take care of the two ends of each part where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other delicately above what rises from the paper of oil, and strain the two cracks from the two parts together; and leave it so for some days, and the skin that has been strained will die and turn dark and peel off, until it falls by itself.

The stitches are made as follows: you take a very fine needle, and put one thread of silk in it, then assemble the threads and tie them together delicately, and make sure that the length of the threads is about the width of your palm; then order another thin thread of silk to pass through the whole thread, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in a healthy place, and expose it to sunlight so that the stitches become visible, because this is a very delicate and fine stitch. Then take the needle and go all around the root of the hair next to the wound, and make a hole in the paper as quickly as you can until you reach the natural hair; then pull out the hair from below the stitches up to the natural hair, and put that hair into the stitches, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand gently until all the hairs come out of the stitches along with the natural hair.

And if the thread is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the thread from underneath all of the thread that you have ordered, until the thread comes out through the pores above and you see it with your own eyes. Then you will pull out the thread and the stitches, and close your eye and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the scar heals; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and lift them up together as they grow longer, and then lift them up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous avons terminé les instructions sur le traitement des poils et que nous sommes maintenant passés à un autre sujet : "la porriture de l'oil".
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or the burning comes into the eye, there are two ways it happens: one natural and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or a fire cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat it is that you break apart this sudden union, and separate its edges, and put in linen poultices, and tie them tight until they are healed; and it does not need that you use in treating it things that dry up and constrict. For if you do that, the illness will return worse than the first one; but there is work with moistening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or almond milk cooked, and ointments made from dissolved wax and any oil, and I put a poultice on it, and cure with those.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you watch out for it so that it does not suddenly close up again in its former form; and these treatments that we have said are nothing other than remedies against this illness returning in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	The fatty substance that comes into the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is under the eye and which is truly called "axacrati", and is of natural origin and accident. The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the way to treat it is that you take a needle, in which there will be one double thread, and stick it into the fatty substance, and make it pierce through both tear ducts, so that the threads come out on either side of the fatty substance. Then tie the fatty substance at the top with the whole needle, and cut off about one finger's width.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure returns in accordance with what is needed, it's good. If not, take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper over, and make two small incisions inside the paper; and have the openings of the two incisions at the two angles of the cut that you made, so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like that of a letter called "one Greek". Then remove the fatty substance, according to how much it is hardened under the paper, then join together the two severed parts and sew them with a linen thread. Then apply the treatments of moistening medicines and poultices until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from an incision or suture or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papyrus, and according to what was said before; then sew between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare devices of all their power with which they make the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs from treatment and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden tearing of the papyrus
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in a way that the paper on top is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or do its natural activities, then it is necessary that you insert the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and use tweezers, as long as you can copy what is written in subtle ink, which is not too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer from ink that is too thick or bleeds into the eye; and make your incision, by which you scrape away this assembled swelling, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and then all of this assembled swelling will be healed, and at no time will it cause a watery discharge in the eye, nor a sweet, nor a sour one; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on top of the eye damp wool soaked in egg white; and after three days cease using the colicor and other sharp things until you are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l'ungue de l'oeil (in English: "of the eyelid of the eye")
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of eyelids: they are nervous and resemble a hard scab, and another that is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture. When you touch it with iron and heat it to burn the splinters, it cannot be done; and both appearances begin near the large tear duct and grow bit by bit until they cover all the eye, its light, and its movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The way of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then you open the eyelids. Lift up the paper with your hand, and hold the eyelid with tweezers of fine stitching, and stretch it upwards. Then take a needle, and put one hair from a horse, or cow, or bull into it, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a bit and stick it through the eyelid, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the eyelid with thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape off all the remaining hairs along the edge of the eyelid where the lashes are, up to the head, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with fine stitches, and leave the natural skin of the tear duct so that by the incision the course of the tears is not accustomed; and at no time stretch the eyelid only on the needle and thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue that is this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the soft tissue does not touch the sensitive skin and break it, and that the lashes are not pierced.
