Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the eyelid is not nervous and you cannot push the needle in, and the stitches cannot enter, this type of eyelid appearance is often cured with medicines; and it grows just like I have described in its division, and if you see it growing, you should operate on the patient's eye, and take out the soft tissue quickly, as sharp as a knife, according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	I cannot provide instructions on how to perform surgery. Is there anything else I can help you with?}

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems like we're still looking at an old medical text from the past.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Some men's eyes are sometimes red, and cover the eyelid and hold steady above the papers and turn to the outside, and seem like a brick rose; and the work is that the patient puts his head in a basin, then works on the eyes, and coils all that flesh into needles suitable for this, and holds it at full strength; then cuts the first skin, and goes cutting with a razor just to the end, and be careful not to hurt the eye during the surgery; and let the incision be as deep as we have said in the incision of the ulcer and in the small forces where one removes the scab, just as the form after this chapter shows it.

des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. de la fistule de l’oil	It seems I was translating a medical text on eye care, specifically related to the removal of external veins from the eye (perhaps a type of eye surgery). The phrase "de la fistule de l'oil" can be translated to English as "of the fistula of the eye". A fistula is an abnormal connection or passageway between two body parts, and in this context, it might refer to a abnormal connection or hole in the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	A "fistule de l'oil" that is not healed by cautery and hot medicine, as I mentioned before, is called an "arissati" fistula. When you cure it with a scalpel and remove all the moist tissue that remains there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then replace it with all of the instrument by which this shape was created; and it is called "sharp head", and it should be made of iron into one head red, and should be pointed like a file so as it is in this present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it back on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a bit as much as you know that this corruption is removed; and do this repeatedly, then restore the place with medicinal ointments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is set, and flesh grows back, and the body of the bowel is set, and it remains like that for 40 days, and it doesn't worsen and isn't inflamed, and there comes no bad accident, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to bring the fistula back to the natural passage according to this form: and it's that you uncover from the bone the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered so take one rod according to this form, and the iron spike should be at three angles, and the shaft should be thinned out up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone next to the abscess, and move your hand away from the wound a little bit. Turn the rod entirely until it pierces the bone, and let the patient feel it through the vein in their neck if they keep their hand on their navel; then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows back and hardens the joint, the matter will go to the navel; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye

When the eyes are open wide and do not bother at all, nor decrease, you should bind the patient; then heal him; then put on him a compress made of aloes, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle; then strain the eye and fill it with bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one in four, and then place one above the other according to the quantity that the eyes need; then bind tightly over with a durable band, and reapply the compresses to suck without hurting; then remove the compresses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the compress becomes moist, you should tighten it; then remove the compress after a day and a night, and if you see the eye restored, it is good; if not, then repeat the dressing and the cloths and the compress and the compresses until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	tear of the vitreous humor

de la bowe de l’oil	From the bottom of the eye.

This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bow in the eye, resembling an arrow descending, and it is not an arrow; and the manner of its appearance during treatment is that you make the patient sit on one seat prepared and straight, then take hold of the head with both hands and pull it so much as to see the bow coming up to your eyes; then tie it fast and do not let it go down and remove the light, and look at the things in front of the patient as he is accustomed; and if it does not come down below, know that it is an arrow, and if the descent of the bow is not aligned as we have said. des aigues de l’oil	This text appears to be a medical description from medieval France, specifically dealing with eye problems. The phrase "des aigues de l'oil" translates to "waters of the eye".
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the marks of the eye in its division and what needs to be pierced; do it according to health. If the eye now bleeds, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Il semble que nous sommes dans une description de pratique médicale ancienne, peut-être issue du Moyen Âge ou de la Renaissance.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the eye by its hardness, for there are some men whose eyes are very hard, then you should take the instrument that is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:

se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. At times, flesh moles are born on the navel, and some of them resemble scorpions in shape. If one has such a mole that it is surrounded by a fine-colored ring, or if it has a soft bone-like color. In that case, where the mole is soft and not ringed, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and close their nostrils, and pour the onion juice onto those moles, and rub them vigorously. Then take what you can grasp with the sharp pointed spatula from one part, as long as you know that the mole is completely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be scraped off, you should open it all up with the sharp and light tools, until nothing is left; and if it's a swelling or a boil, if the scab comes off as it should, and if they are malignant boils, then hasten to cauterize them until the scab is dried out and the moles are completely removed. Then pour on oil, vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the navel opening is not open and there are moles coming out just to the edge of the mouth, know that it is cured; and if the moles do not come out as they should, know that there are moles in the bone above, where the tools cannot reach. Then you must insert a thread of linen, not too thick, with your hands, leaving between each node about one finger's width or less. And have the patient put the ends of the thread into their navel to some power, and pull on them fragrantly until it comes out through the mouth; and this is often done by children in school, and it is a simple thing for those who want to do it. Then take the head that comes out through the navel with one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them out slowly while holding onto the thread. Do this until you know that the moles have corrupted the tissue, then pull out the thread, drain the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back into the navel as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the tissue; and then put a poultice on the navel for some time until it is cured, and if necessary use dry medicines; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the chief, from which oils and medicines are distilled into the navel.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or alum, resembling an open lamp like a flask, and it conducts in the same way; and if you see one, make a closed flask, and it should have instruments for purging the chief; and it should have a handle at the top to hold it when heating oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises on the navel, and grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to look at. And in order to cure it, you should remove it at the beginning, and take out all its roots; then apply hot cautery or burning medicine to it. If one waits too long to remove it until it has grown large, beware of the fact that it may be hard, have a fine color, and poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected boil, for when you cut into it even once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the boil is of soft touch, not of fine color, and one sees that it can be completely removed, then empty the patient's body and the boil's roots patiently, and treat the area with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cleaned out
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous joints, it is beneficial for little, more than in some people. So when this happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh and still bleeding with all its blood; and then press the two lips together at a seam, and let it heal until it is cured. And if the lips are already dried on one side and the other, you should scrape off all the parts of their crust as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips together at a seam, and bind them, and powder on top powdered dragon's blood and incense powder; and put on the powders a piece of strong plasters or another binding plaster, and let it be until it cracks by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching the wound is that you assemble the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the belly wound stitching; or with a thread, as I have already told you.
des apostemes des levres	of boils on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have within their lips a hard boil, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger ones. Then it is necessary to turn the lips inside out, and cut on each node, and take them with pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the area after the incision, made from vitriol powder, until the scab is dried up; and then apply oil, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a piece of gum tissue attached to the gums appears, which the ancients called "albulus". It is necessary that you hold it with forceps and cut at its root, and let the bleeding or scab dry out; then put on the area vitriol powder or other binding and drying powders. And if that piece of gum tissue comes back after the incision, and many times appears, you should cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back again after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments to cut.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and bitter; and sometimes they are black and greenish-yellow and worm-like, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling. It is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and their jaws be in your holy place, and remove the teeth or scabs where they appear, until nothing remains; and similarly do with blackness and greenness and yellowness and other stains, until they are removed; and if at first cause one removes them, it is good; but if not, repeat the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because the raspers used to remove the teeth from outside have different shapes than those used to remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay as long as you can from extracting it, because this should not be done; for it is a very high procedure, and one must have no excuse for doing so.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to extract it, you should be certain about the healthy tooth. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it's the healthy tooth that hurts, and have the bad tooth extracted; but in any case, the pain does not go away until the bad root is removed, because we have already said this to the doctors. And when you are well certain about the healthy tooth, you should scrape around the tooth on all sides with a sharp instrument to protect the gum from all parts; then move it to your hands or forceps with fine tips at the first notch and notch, until they are well closed; then tighten the forceps tightly; and the patient's jaws should be in your holy place between your knees, and hold them still so that they don't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it doesn't come out easily, you should take one of these instruments and gently push it into place from each side lightly, and then remove it as you did at first. And if the tooth is pierced and torn, you should fill it with thread, in the places where the perforations are; and if you need to use fine forceps to grasp it, so that it doesn't break when you pull on it; and you must work very carefully around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And do it well in mind that you don't break the tooth and leave a part behind, and that it will come back to the patient with greater pain from the root of the tooth than the first time. And beware that you don't act like the ignorant doctors who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the root, and do not bring about what we have told; but sometimes bring on great diseases through the roots that remain or because they break the root, as we have often said. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, oil, and salt; and if there are decorations of blood that come out, which often happen, apply a poultice of vitriol powder to the area; and if that doesn't help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tweezers, through which you must remove the teeth first, are with long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when you pull them, and be made of good iron well-made, and have teeth to firmly hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in place, you should put on the location moistened cotton wool, i.e. for a day or two, until the site is softened, then insert the pliers which are called "algefri", through which the gum looks like that of a suckling; and they be made inside as well as a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and I put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a plane, through which this is their shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; if not, you help with all the pliers, through which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with that instrument which has two jaws, through which this is their shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fixings that are in front of the reason for the teeth, and this instrument which looks like large pliers, through which this is their shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is strong so that it cannot break, and you know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of cases, and they do not break the jaw or the other bones, if they can help it, then they search for the instruments that I have told you about, and they ask for gestures, through which this is their shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be strong and hold well so that the bone does not slip away, but rather can hold and remove it; and then restore the place to medicines suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, you should use all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape and the form is ugly, and especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be polished or filed: then pull it. And if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument through which this is its shape, and it looks like a small beak, and is made of iron with a sharp point at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, take this file through which this is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file through which we make needles; and gently file the tooth in short strokes, so that it does not move until it is smooth. Then take the plane at the end of all this scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you need to file the sharpness so that it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the word:
quant li dent lochent	Quand il sont déchiquetés. (When they are chipped)
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth are chipped, either by percussion or by falling, and the disease cannot be pressed over them without causing a fracture, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, but that is not enough; then they need to be restrained with a thread of gold, because silver threads become green and rotten, but gold does not change; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you see the teeth loose, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the coverage up to the part where you started, and stretch your hand subtly and wisely, until they do not move anymore. And make sure the thread is tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the thread with a pair of pliers, and assemble them, and reinsert them between the healthy teeth, and place them in such a way that they do not hurt the tongue; and then leave them tight as long as possible, and if they come loose or the threads rot, tighten them with another thread. If it stays this way and serves for all its time, this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, then put it back in its place, fresh and fresh, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and patient meddle with it. And at times a shape like that of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the spot where the defect is, and it is tightened just as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At no time is this ligament that comes from under the tongue by nature, which one is born with, or as an accident of a healed wound, excepted. The procedure is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your healthy hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament of the large part, so that the tongue is detached from its dwelling place. And if there is hardness or scabbing, and it's a sudden healing of the wound, put the thread and stitch the wide part; and make sure the opening is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath. And when you have done this, lift the place with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then apply under the tongue a linen tent; and the patient will clean it every night, so that the wound does not heal.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling is of a color that is white or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is an ulcer; and if it is declining towards pus, and there is moisture, inject oil, and make a fine poultice around it, and deliver him from one part to another; and if blood flows into your work, put on vinegar compress as long as it is stopped up, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the bad matter; then raise the place of silk and linen, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Never once comes a swelling from within the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the .ij. almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard swelling of small size and white color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for the bleeding; but leave it alone until it dies, and then you will cut it off, or it would break on its own; and if it is of pale color and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to scrape, but look first if the swelling has cooled down and is calm. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and your hands be clean, and open his mouth and take the servants between his hands, and press the tongue under all the instrument, which is its shape; and it should be of fine silver or lead as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the swelling, then take a thorn and insert it into the almond, and draw out the bad matter from above as much as you can; and remove any thread or string that may be attached, then scrape off with the instrument, which is its shape, resembling a forceps. And although its head is curved, one end to the other, and are very sharp, and it's made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, then scrape off with pincers, which is its shape.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be pointed on one side and flat on the other. And when you have scraped one of the almonds, scrape the other in the same way, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and vinegar, and warm oil, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or cooked apple peelings, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped. Then cure it as long as it takes to heal; and once swelling appears in the throat other than the two almonds, then scrape them both in the same way as the first two.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for a swelling that had appeared in her throat, which was a swelling of the epiglottis. It had grown so large that it had closed off the entire throat and she couldn't breathe or eat, and would have died within a day or two if it hadn't been treated immediately.
de l’uve	of the urine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When urine flows to the urethra and it is long and straight, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen and round, it is called "urethra". When it is cut in a way that we have said in the division, and the incision does not help, and you see that the growth on the penis is calmed down, and it is subtle, then it needs to be cut; and that which is round and assembled but not long; and it is bloody or of dark color or black, then it needs to have the incision closed. For there is great danger over the patient. Then, when you see it, according to the way I said, in terms of its shape and length, the patient should sit before the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we mentioned beforehand; then insert the needle into the urethra and remove any excess, and cut with one or two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two testicles. And you need to not cut too much beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it will cause pain to the voice and words; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then you should use a trick to cauterize the area without causing fear. The manner of cauterization is with sharp vinegar. And it is that the patient puts his head on your hand, and then presses the tongue against the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and mix with live charcoal, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and insert the handle of this instrument into the urethra
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a head of hair or some kind of stick to hold the medicine, just like a spoon's handle, and place the instrument on top of the medicine in the urethra; and have the patient sit comfortably with his chest up, so that the saliva and mucus from his mouth flow into the medicine inside, but not down to the throat or the wound. Then take your hand and press the medicine onto the urethra for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it turn black and the irritation from the medicine is calmed; and if you need to, take some cotton and wrap it around a tool, and moisten the cotton with medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the tube on top, until the cotton gets warm inside the urethra. And do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry out, and after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to re-start the cauterization of the medicine, start again, and after that, clear out the area around the urethra with cotton soaked in butter, and clean up anything around the medicine; and be careful not to burn yourself with cold water, and be cured with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization, and if it is cured through fumigation in this manner, take camphor, yarrow, origanum, rue, chamomile, and wormwood, and gather all or some of these herbs together in one pot, and put oil in the pot, and make it boil. The pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have a hollow instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Whether it is of silver or copper, and whether one of the keys is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapour rises to the eye through the tube, as long as the eye is numbed; afterwards it often recurs, as long as the tube is dry, take care not to do this at the beginning of the coming of hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do this until the decline of hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put an egg-cod inside it, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; because the egg-cod does not let the vapour harm the mouth, and it is good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times one has seen it to be at the throat or the spine of a fish, or nothing at all; so you must try what you see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see what the thing is; and what does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it's necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will expel the bad thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of nail, or a root of lettuce, or one quarter of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes up, it will be cured, and you'll have done better; and if it doesn't come out from what we've said, then take a instrument of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted upwards. Be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything goes wrong or you push the bone inside; and it's better if the patient themselves puts the instrument in, for they will know if the thing is being expelled; if they put it down, or pull it out at the entire instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La première partie du texte semblait décrire une technique de traitement médical pour une affaissement ou un blocage à l'échelle des poumons, et maintenant il semble que le sujet soit la "sansue" (ou plutôt, la sève) de la gorge. Je n'ai pas d'informations claires sur ce que pourrait être cette "sansue", mais je suppose qu'il s'agit d'un terme médical anachronique qui désignait une sorte de liquide ou de flux issu de la gorge.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the disease is medicine with the sweat, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not benefit, then examine the throat of the patient in the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you. And if you see the disease, so treat all one little inch or with delicate tongs that are worth those things. And if they are not worth it, take a hair cord, and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the head of the cord on a hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient feels cold all day, then take a full cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and spit out in its presence without swallowing, and move it to your hand often; and as soon as the disease senses the water, it will disappear.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not disappear as we said, then fumigate the patient with aloes, at the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will go away without lingering. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot where there are glowing coals, and the cover of the pot should be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and through these holes should be the ends of the instrument; then throw your fumigation into the pot, and the patient puts the head of the cord in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the disease; and now the disease will go away, and if it does not disappear, you can repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient drink, eat salty things and other things, but do not make them drink water; and then it is necessary for the illness to come out through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	It seems that the text you provided is a medieval medical text, likely from the 13th or 14th century. The language and style are characteristic of Old French, specifically the Middle French dialect.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many kinds of abscesses are described in this book as they appear after a while on one side and the other, and they differ in their holes and shapes; and there are two ways in which one is like itself, and because of moisture. And the second way is for those that are in the body's members. For the abscess of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the abscess of a well-nourished area is different from that which appears in joints, and each has its own judgment in work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the flesh is dead according to their completion; and those who need to be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like an abscess near a joint. For when abscesses come near joints, and you leave them until they are putrid around them, it may happen that the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is thoroughly dead, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, then pierce it when it is dead; and do not pierce a ripe abscess without digestion being completed, unless it is one that is near the foundation, lest it putrefy inside and become an ulcer; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for piercing an abscess that is dead according to completion, and it is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the quieting of the movement and inflammation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation where it depends more on the location of the abscess, and where it opens into a cavity; and the piercing should be made with a long instrument, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those who suffer from them, the swelling occurs in the adjacent member. And when an abscess is located in the flesh of the body, it is necessary to wait until it is confirmed to be digested and completed, as we have said. For if you lance it before then, the body will be filled with venom from it, and be full of foul matter; and perhaps the edges and the depth of it will harden. And if there is an abscess that is incised according to the length of the body, according to what the member requires. And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many cracks according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to sew up the skin, and cover; when it has become as much like a flagon, and is flattened, then it is necessary to do just as one does for babies: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such where you cover just like the leaves of mirtle, like abscesses of angles; and if there are such where you make a circular incision, and other cuts and similar coverage.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, like a soft and superficial abscess, it is necessary that you lance it thoroughly. And when the abscess is large, and has formed a significant swelling, and you lance it, you should not pull out all of the pus at once, but rather pull out part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then pull out anything that remains; do this repeatedly several times, until the swelling has come out completely. Even if the patient is weak in constitution, or a woman, or small children, or old men who are decrepit. For the hope of healing can sometimes be shaken with the issue of the pus, so that by chance the patient may die, and you may not perceive it. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have lanced your abscess, close the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, then bring linens or old cotton to it; and if it's a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then it is necessary that you sew each one with a linen bag so that they come together; and if you have stitched in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or the rags of linen soaked in moisture, and tie it up until the next day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound from surgery becomes infected and festers, then bring cold and clear water, and a damp cloth, and apply it to the sore wound several times. And if the infection of the wound persists, then bring medicine and ointment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is summer time, and the wound or abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary that you place on damp cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it's autumn time, and the wound is fatty, then it is necessary that you place on damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the next day, as we have said. And then untie the abscess and clean it out and cure it, as it becomes necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is necessary to understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must go before the treatments of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or swellings come from small abscesses, and are ways in which pus is contained, just as the silk of a hen's egg, and there are many similarities. There are those that are fatty and like polyps, with moisture also; and some like that which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery has done it contrarily. And the operation of cutting it is such that you use an instrument called "entromissoire", from which its shape comes as follows, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, do it above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, then dry-skin without leaving any remaining skin, for it will return again if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and then reinsert the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know well that it does not remain from night to night; then cure the wound with ointment as necessary, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds one night full of pus, cut it according to this shape, lengthwise; and insert your finger and empty it completely, and put all your care in extracting the pus from the place where it resides; and if the artery has done it contrarily, do what I told you afterwards. And similarly with the abscess if it is stony, and hard to cut, and to cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony and moist abscess is lighter, for it is full of blood. And there are some of these abscesses on the head or without moisture, and among them was one abscess that I cut from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, sharp and white, and could not break it; and if you were to make any incision on it, you would have done as well in making a wound with a stone. In other abscesses coming from the head, especially those that come from the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the operation should always be most dependent on the location, so that the bow can come out; and cure them as necessary.
des scrophules	Of swellings.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	There are many times that this swelling occurs in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they move around and come together. And each scrophule is properly contained within its own space, just like the boil and swelling of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these swellings are many. There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and do not obey health. So when you see one with a good disposition to touch it, and it resembles the color of the body, and is movable from each part and is not hard against the neck or the artery or the channel, and is not deep; then you should cover it up, and scrape off each part, and use the two lips of the knife if you need them, as we have said in head swellings; and pull it out slowly and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor touch the spatula's edge or blade, so that your hands escape and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not leave you working, then pour vitriol on the wound, or some powder that prevents bleeding, and tightens the wound; and let it sit until the swelling is calmed down and the wound becomes soft and begins to rot. And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work, completing it as much as possible. Then examine yourself to see if there are any small scrophules remaining, and cut them out and clean them.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scab, it is necessary that you sew together the two lips of the wound, and now bind them, then there will be no remaining redundancy because of the size of the scab. It is necessary that you take care to cut out the root of it, and pull it hard, and bind it as we have said. Those scabs that hold redundancy, pierce them where they are most dead; and pierce in like manner as the one previously mentioned, underneath, then add tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply a salve to the wound dripping fat, until it be healed.
de squinance	Squince.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting out of the throat; but I never saw in our land one who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squince, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglote" be severed; and that one not help by these things, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are at those who have apoplexy warm in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two parts.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cut out the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four a small cut through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut from side to side, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and let it be such that if it is suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis then there is no fat and the veins are long enough.
