et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these piercings that have gone there is no strong cure except operation, and the vanity of foolish surgeons who meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which has not pierced and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proved.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and is that the sick person lies between your hands on their back; and lifts up their legs as high as their buttocks, and has their buttocks inclined to their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put an iron tube in, or a lead one if there is twisting, as long as you know where the intestine comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the sick person feels it around their fundament, then it is good that you put your index finger in.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if they sense then that the intestine has been pierced; and it is discovered where you feel between your finger's tip and the flesh, at that point know that it is piercing.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if there is no bulging or swelling, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is always said that some can be well healed, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help we give is that we reheat the fine cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot in the fistula, as long as it reaches near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those charred pieces are burnt, which are like a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the healing comes from moistened tubes in butter, as long as those charred pieces come out, and then the healing comes from anointing with ointment that is greasy and closing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it has been healed in this way, then it's well. If not, then otherwise it cannot be healed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the intestine comes in and does not pierce all the way to the fundament, and there is a thick covering of flesh or skin between your finger and the intestine, and you see the fistula at what comes out from under this covering of skin, then...
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and insert it immediately before the intestine, and then burn the cauterizer afterwards, as far as it reaches to the head of the intestine.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the intestine will be delivered and healed. Then cut out those charred pieces that resemble a bird's feather, and there will remain nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound swells up, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cauterizer of fire unites two opposing things: that is to say, the burning of those charred pieces stuck together, and the drying out of blood and moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then heal with moistened tubes in butter or fresh cheese, as long as the abscess discharges pus, and the charred pieces come out through the wound.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then heal the wound with anointing ointments that are thickening and drying out, and which are known as dry medicine.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes right down to the fundament and is far from the body, then stick your finger into the fundament and inspect it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the intestine and between them is the skin or flesh or charred flesh, near where it will pierce, then there should be no more than a spark of hope and faith, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you burn it as we have said, or you cut it right to the bottom, or if you burn and then insert tubes and treat it in the first way.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the intestine that holds the fundament, and the evacuations come out through the unnatural passage.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then heal it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps then it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it afterwards, since it has been cut near the fundament, by a tube or by another instrument pointed for this purpose.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cut out that charred piece which is in the wound, as far as you can see.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to close the fistula in the part far from the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the sick person.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And there is no fistula that follows this way, and so when you insert the intestine into the fistula, it is in the proximity of the fundament, near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a tube with a hole at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and insert one twisted thread in two, and insert the tube into all the thread in the fistula as far as it goes to the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the edge of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from the pierced one, just as you insert your finger or fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw out the head of the thread, and join together the two heads together, and tie one to the other, and leave it for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and then restrain it no more, as long as the thread cuts through those charred pieces that are between them and separate.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is sutured and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it to pierce in all ways that you can, as long as it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a hole that is too deep and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine of the thorn from which one makes the fistula is very narrow and pointed.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side it is not, therefore one does not cut those that one must not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the curved ones.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	The emorydes are according to two manners: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in cutting them blood comes out.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more of them, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have less moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and in cutting them out or one small drop of yellow water or a small drop of blood comes out, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the fundament is to command the sick person to strain so as to bring them out into chambers, until the fundament empties and they appear in threads.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, then hold it with forceps or between your finger and thumb, and cut off at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the forceps cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them up on a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and draw them out with your fingers, then cut them off, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cauterizing.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you burn them as is said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot come out, then purify the sick person with a harsh and biting clyster to wash away what is in the fundament, so that it may come out openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the sick person's pain subsides and the thread comes out of the fundament, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you grasp them with your finger or forceps and cut them off, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that the sick person does not dread the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you make the stitch in this way: take one twisted thread and insert it into a needle, and then draw out the thread above and make the needle to pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread around the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and it should be of good size; and then bind the thread tightly, tie the knot, pull out the needle, and do in this way with all the others, leaving one for correction of the superfluity of blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the fundament, and command the sick person to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it alone until they are quiet, and when they are still, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the drying up of the fundament or fundament's opening.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of the fundament in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the sickness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you remove with a thorn or your finger the scab on top, which does not let it moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat him until he is healed as it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot heal, then scrape more strongly than before, until he becomes quite healed and scabbed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is completely healed.
dou fremit	from the flux.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	formication is a small burned appearance on the skin, and goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the flesh, and feels just as numb from flux, and comes to all parts of the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a wick from an owl's feather or a strong goose quill, and put that wick on the flux, until the red circles encircle the flux entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around to grab the whole wick until you cut it all around the flux, and put it deep in, and extract the flux from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, then do as with a thread of silver or iron according to this shape, and make it subtle below and draw it above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and squeeze it hard. And if you see it, then burn the flux as is said in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or gold, or molten and beaten metal, and sometimes one makes those small and large instruments according to which they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is as follows: above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has two perforations, one above where the belly is tied, as you see, and one inside pierced with the thread, and on each side there are two holes, and on the other one hole.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it is tied to the belly where one places the medicine in a bladder of an animal or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has between each hole a small space, then insert into these holes one strong thread of twisted wire in ten or twelve turns, and bind the belly as a goat is bound.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, and clysterize; and this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the tip of the clyster with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister should grasp the clyster with both hands together until it is completely empty, then pull out the clyster, and lift up the sick person's legs towards the bed.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine needs to come out, then tie him up as tightly as possible; and if he sleeps one entire night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him in the disease of purging of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or swelling, then the clyster should be just as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the subtle clyster on which the skin is strained.
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by hitting with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, or with a spear or fist or seat, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or they are made according to the places of the body, such as wounds that cut on the neck, or head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will start with simple head wounds, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from hitting with a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly about applying a hot poultice: if you do it at once to heal the wound from the head itself, even if there is a small drop of blood from the wound, and the healing is contrary to the part that is hurt.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and take away the sick person's repletion of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not want to heal, then reduce his food, and do not let him drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a poultice on the wound, if an abscess comes, with a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or vinegar only.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood and hasn't been changed by air or powder, what I'll say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has become inflamed, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot come together by themselves, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone and tender, and only holds by a small amount, then cut it off; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the sick person to eat thick meats, such as roasted capons and bread, also chickens and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find purulence in the skin that is not near the bone, then cut out all the purulence and throw it away, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound that is not covered and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put in this powder which heals at once when the inflammation has subsided.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take equal parts of incense, dragon's blood, and living calcined lime, and pound it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill the wound with this powder, and bind it tightly until it dries well and unites with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then tie it well, and let it be untied when it is no longer swollen, because one does not remove the medicine until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes we do this with lime alone, when we don't have incense or dragon's blood, but the inflammation has already made the wound swell.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the inflammation has already made the wound swollen, especially in the flesh, then one does not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments or pastilles made from wheat flour and water and honey, until it drips with pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave it alone and not apply any constraining thing, because it hurts the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as calcined lime dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and they have a sharp edge and are full of pus, then puncture or cut them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and hemorrhage comes from it, then uncover it, clean it, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the conduit is kept, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the nerve on top of the throatbone, and don't touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then strain it properly, and let it alone for some days, then cure it with old ointments as long as it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, sew it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can take them all out, and those that you cannot take out, then let them be until the wound rots.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and it should be cleaned and tied the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then cure it thus as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the stab wound or cut
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a stab wound or cut and the wound is deep, look to see if there is any sign of windiness or bubbling in the evil-smelling discharge: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, then put no powder on it in the first hour nor tie it for the blood that will not congeal deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and the patient revives at heart and the sickness dies away.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on attractive ointment and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep over the wound three days, or four days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor bad trembling of the heart and no signs of tetanus.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good indications, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it then with tincts and other treatments, until he is sound again.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and becomes ulcerated, then know that there is a fistula; treat it thus as one must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and it is superficial, or worse, or in the back, then treat as one would the wound in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, dress with stitches; and if it is small, treat with powder; and if it has been pressed into the bone and has splintered pieces, then clean out the wound and remove the fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislodged, then let the wound suppurate, for it will ease the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is thus as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a broken or ruptured uterus
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the womb are great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound there comes out sometimes the intestines or the membranes of the intestines, by which their introduction is known.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the treatment is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound heals worse than the great one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore one sews up the intestines with more pins, unless they are sewn together hot in hot.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately as soon as they feel cold, so they cannot be sewn up with pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to leave the middle-sized wound open, because one can sew up the intestine to its place in two days.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the womb is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the womb,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and notwithstanding they are more proper with the stitch of the womb, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine comes out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if there is anything to put in, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from being cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	moisten a sponge or one soft cloth in hot water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in hot water with squinat and cypress and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and anoint the intestine until the swelling is gone.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes it becomes so swollen that it only needs to be broken in order to deflat.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, then moisten the intestine with hot water or broth and let it cook until the meat is cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this the entrance to the wound is eased of much pain.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is better than cutting.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without a great necessity that there is no other way.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so as to cut from within in the curve and not outwards, and see what shape it takes.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine comes out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its place as naturally as possible.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are unable to do so, because it is better that way.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	then it is advisable that you make the patient lie on their back on a raised surface.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and have his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and similarly if the rupture of the womb is in one of the two lower parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then you should make an effort so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is advisable to take heed of what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	In small wounds, do what you think best,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands one of those skilled ministers who knows the whole rupture by hand.
et assemble les levres;	and sew up the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or more, according to the size and breadth of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound a good two inches empty, and stick in a needle there where it has a good strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two points of the needle.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, until you make it penetrate from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and sew up the two ends of the needle in four stitches.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then twist a doubled thread around the needle from both sides.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then sew up the two lips of the wound properly.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another good two inches empty, and stick in another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread so that you have done with the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to make them in this way according to the number of needles you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be thin and thick, of medium size,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is advisable that they be of medium size.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not advise to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and open up the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I wrap cloths or rags around the ends of the needles so that they hold in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is stitched together.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more advisable in small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it only requires one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you sew together the two heads of the skin and the two ends of the needle in one, with a strong thread of medium size.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these three heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then tie the thread at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews a dress.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave space between each stitch, the thickness of a little finger's width.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is called "at home".
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitched a wound that was in the stomach of a man.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been wounded by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than the width of a hand.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were hanging down by two hands' width.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I pulled it back into place and let it rest for 24 hours before stitching it.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed in 15 days, and the patient was cured and whole again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I didn't cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where you couldn't find any, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed old cotton on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper manners of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced through the skin from right to right, then tie the thread or cord with which you have pushed in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inner part through to the outer part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew in the same way as a furrier sews furs.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you leave the thread on one side and take it up again from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galien calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to sew the two parts together naturally, like those who assemble them.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one of the ends of the thread to the other end, in the same way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	stick a needle or thread close by and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with the two ends of the thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part, in two other threads that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the more common and better manner of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien himself says these words, and everyone testifies to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must put one needle from this side and the other from that side, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is on the abdomen,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as if the heat had changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the bowel, and on top of that put a powdering substance of drying flesh.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the heat has changed it, then apply some ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tighten the thread and stitch together the skin and the flesh.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound just like the others, until it is cured and whole again.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on old cotton, as soon as it starts to heal well.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you don't need any other medicine besides these, in most simple cases of wounds.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will become a community (a gathering of pus) with main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	it is advisable to boil linen lightly in hot temperate oil or rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the edges and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it smells bad or feels pain in the belly and returns many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then perform a purging with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the stench comes close to the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot be healed if it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the delicacy of their vessels and the subtlety of all the body, and the approach to its nature from the navel.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out of the wound, put it back inside just like the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, it is advisable that you tie the part that is black so that blood does not come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are vessels and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from the part under the wound until outside to ease the extraction when the intestine bursts and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some people.
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the abdomen by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach.
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became ulcerated and formed an abscess, and there came out from it purulence and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him according to what I knew, and I didn't stop subtletizing until he was healed, and the wound closed up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient would have a problem in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm to him, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking normally.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and the experienced ones said that when someone has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take from the thread of strong hemp, then sew together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has closed up the mouth, put it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it holds its mouth shut.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cut the thread, and it stays like this so that it cannot be undone.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another thread behind in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That thread holds fast in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread which has been freed from its entrails,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie one fine twisted linen thread to the end of that intestinal thread.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle and sew up the intestine, and tie it in the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with thread is not far from the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an ulcer or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes ulcerated, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when it is hardened and heals well.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to its hard, firm, and white nodule, where there is no pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also as hard as the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and at one time it bursts clear and clean, and at another time it becomes more compact.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and at another time quite large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have said in the division of wounds that any wound which is not healed and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of the blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its bad quality.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is rotten and the matter has bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine used in the treatment is not good.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague or pestilence.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property of the region causes delayed digestion and slow healing, and tends to follow its natural course.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because there are vessels or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or from the thread, intestine, bladder, or any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or from the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it has such a quality that comes to the principal part of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this manner are of serious healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you are confident of the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you recognize it, then take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, then search;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of gold.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the gold folds bend around the twistingness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	so search by inserting a catheter through one of the perforations.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture comes from one perforation to another, and it cleanses;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then search by lancet according to your knowledge if there is bone or nerve, and be careful in the depth.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and excise the defective and corrupted parts that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then close it so that it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well located in a straight place, then cut to the depth, as far as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put dampened tents of medicinal dough, and bandage just up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine eats away the excess matter that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put on salves of good fat, until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if they are not healed by these means, then cauterize them as we have said;
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not interfere with your cutting of the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, then scrape out all the corruption.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then close it with good fat salve until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, then return to the same procedure as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the bottom;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it is uncovered and you search until you are at the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	And if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot come near;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there's no other remedy than to let it heal by its own nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is only a small piece of bone corrupted, and you can grasp it with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then pull it out with an instrument suitable for this purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture prevents you from pulling them out, and there's no room for error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut through the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then apply something antiseptic to the wound;
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it so until the area around the bones is thoroughly purified.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then you will have an easier time removing them.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as from the thigh or leg,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape out all the corruption and blackness that surrounds the bone.
puis restoure la plaie;	then repair the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted matter that comes close to the surface of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it's necessary to scrape and cut all the way up to the corruption, and then close it once it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of an abscess that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and receive help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from an internal cause within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	such that the matter came to the leg and was inflamed with a large abscess, and had no way to open up;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but by their foolishness they cut so high that the abscess burst open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and much matter came out and it became an ulcer, and there were many sinuses that all discharged forth and outward from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons applied treatment for two years, and there was no skilled surgeon in their craft.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medications with which they were treating him;
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what was coming out through the sinuses was of great bulk.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man was becoming red and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a tent into one of these sinuses, and then searched out all the sinuses.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were all connected to each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hastened and cut into one of the sinuses until I exposed a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be corrupted and perforated, with the corruption coming right up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped out what appeared of the corrupted bone, and I believed that there was no other corruption beyond what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to repair the wound with suitable medications for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I tried again, and found the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption had continued in the bone, and I scraped it out, then removed it, and began to close up the area.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not close it until I cut around about the length of a hand's palm of the bone, and removed all the way to its edge.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I repaired it with medicine, and it was quickly healed and closed up.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not need to be re-done except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For during the evacuation it would often bleed profusely, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone, there grew hard flesh, and he was in good health and suffered no harm or contraindication from anything, either before or after.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be scraped out in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and stretch it to the top of the open bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to hold it in place at the top.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another linen cloth, larger than the first one, and tie it on top of the flesh that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch out the top so that you can pull out the corrupted flesh beneath.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the spot where you see it can be scraped, making sure not to cut the healthy flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot iron or a heated spatula under the bone to loosen and remove the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and scrape it as far as you can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it;
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape out from one part to the other the corruption, and make sure the scraping is as long as the length of the corruption, just as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and scrape out the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of both joints, then there's no other remedy but to cut it out.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the elbow of the hand or the knee, then that thing is very strong and difficult to cut out.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you should investigate that corruption and find out how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but without harming the adjacent vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and be aware that the knife and the scraping tools to cut these bones are many, depending on the size of the bone and its appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary to prepare at each resemblance of work its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and be aware that the work will show you the instrument needed, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think of the instrument you need, according to what is necessary.
dou feu	and from fire (to sterilize and purify).
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can be damaged or become diseased either from an internal cause or from an external cause.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated the corruption with medicinal treatment and it does not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut that member right down to where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes by cutting out the corruption or the evil, which is greater than the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackening, the corruption of the member spreads from limb to limb.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the whole body; so hasten with the cutting.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar creatures.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the vein, then cut it out, and do not give him any space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut it out at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it out at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is the death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there's no remedy better than cutting off the amount of its evilness.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do exactly the same thing when the corruption comes to the foot; if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, then cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there's no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or scraping out the member is that you tie it on top and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one servant down with one ligature, and another servant up with the other ligature.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh between the two ligatures to the width of one spatula, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you cut or scrape it out, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the scraping does not touch the healthy area.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another abscess and pustule come to the patient's wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if a flow of blood comes out while you are working, then cauterize the area quickly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put some constricting powders on it, then come back to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in Somerset:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a blackening that seemed like burning from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the corruption came first in his foot vein, until it had spread throughout the whole foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corruption came back in the vein of his hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him medicines which were supposed to be helpful after cleansing the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wished that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of reacting the material.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he was desperate, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other remedy than what we use when we must amputate something.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and stays for so long that it gathers a large collection of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it rots and bursts, and the pus comes out, and leaves the area empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is on top is as thin as a delicate cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not spread to the bone or the nerve, and such an illness is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it's not called a "fistula" either.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must cut around the whole skin, and at the same time when it is thin, like a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not harden from its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have confidence that the skin has hardened, and the corruption is not deep in the bone.
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick like flesh, then cleanse it with a purge in this way:
