regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	check if the abscess is large, and the pus that comes out of it has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse him with Egyptian medicine made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloe, oil, and lye, equal parts, and put the mixture in a vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	so that the medicine is red and thickens to the consistency of honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take as much of it as you need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the abscess with this mixture, and tie up the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine act for two hours, then express it by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the abscess is cleaned and the pus is expelled.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is cleansed with ash water.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not available, and you take ashes of grapevine wood, and pour water over them.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it, and cleanse with it, until you know that the abscess is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then cleanse him with a mixture of water and honey, with a little bit of burnt lye.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or cleanse him with a mixture of honey and sweet wine, which has the property to clean and wash.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the flesh harden.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and are confident that the abscess is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then cleanse him with a mixture that makes new flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take diaphinite plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or cleanse him with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned earlier or how to make ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the abscess is small and the tube of the catheter cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then stretch it open with a iron rod a little bit, and put in a tent made of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam oil, so that it is stretched out.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave just enough space for the catheter to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that spouts pus is on top, then cut or move it down to where you want it to be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is deep inside, it doesn't allow for new flesh to grow.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you can't cut out the abscess from below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare it in such a way that the pus runs down to the lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep inside, there's no new flesh allowed to grow.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you can't cut out the abscess from below as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then prepare it in that way: so that the pus runs down lightly and doesn't let any of the pus remain.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the abscess,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and spread it over a linen cloth that covers the whole abscess.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut out from the strongest side of the abscess, a little bit larger than the first one.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then spread soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the abscess's opening to relieve the pus, and don't remove the large cloth until after a few days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that one on top of the abscess's opening is often removed to let out the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and be aware of what comes out of the pus, whether it's venom or blood or a clot or digestive or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and pay attention to whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that comes out of the abscess on the skin,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the abscess has hardened, and approach healing.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then release it in the morning or on the third day, and when you open the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the milk flows with undigested blood for many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons cut through the skin after a long time, do not lose hope of recovery.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are men whose wounds take a long time to heal, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested blood shoots out from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and becomes hardened, add medicinal substances that are moist in nature but dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as refined oil of vitriol, for it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take refined oil and mix it with rose oil, and add the juice of old equalized wine.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same for thickened boiled honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when refined oil is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and pound them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then anoint the cloth with it, and apply it to the breast, and do not administer any other ointment for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of heavenly lily, which is also like flour of aloes and cinnamon;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and make use of simple or compound medicines: pound them, and make powder from them, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is in deep, and has made impression on the bone, or hard members, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the abscess is not effective, as we said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil or pustule on the finger.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Painrice (or Panarice) is a boil that appears under the nail of the thumb.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or under the toe, or perhaps it occurs in other toes.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and becomes old, if it comes to a thick boil.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and run and spread pus as long as the nail root of the finger is being destroyed, and perhaps it will destroy it all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to corruption just up to the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the swelling of the toe is large, and the color is bluish-green.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut off all the remaining superfluous part of the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail is inflamed with flesh and begins to rot and bleed,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a hot iron under the nail that is infected with flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and close it tightly on top, and carefully and gently cut out the inflamed flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh medicinal ointments that are burning and corrosive in order to remove it all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut out the infected part and treat with fire, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it will not heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the toe corrupting, then cut it off at the joint just as it was said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering and suppurating, and you feel great pain, then it is necessary that you let it heal first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the spurting abscess diagonally upwards.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not come to the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something on top that will soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the ear in the hand (i.e. a type of swelling or inflammation).
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fistula that occurs on the hands of some people, perhaps it is all fleshly.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps it has a bone or a nail inside, and sometimes it has no cartilage at all.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them occur in the root of the joint, or the birth is in certain toes of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that occur in any part of the hand do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that occur at the joint of the hand, perhaps they can move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the swelling of one who is all fleshly is light, in a similar way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it out from its root with a wide abscess.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that occur at the root of the joint are grievous to cure, and you should hesitate before cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	When one occurs near the end of the finger or thumb, it is necessary to cut out the surrounding flesh up to the bone first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread for that place, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that occurs on the fingers together comes from birth, or a boil, or scorching by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out the swelling, and then repair the finger according to its natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or wet cloths soaked in rosed oil so that they do not become swollen again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen until the place is solidly healed, just as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on any of his fingers with the palm, cut out that swelling in the way it is necessary.
Des vils	A pause or a blank line, often used to indicate a change in topic or a break in the text. In this case, it seems like we've reached the end of this particular passage about swellings on the hands and fingers.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Flesh boils are large, swollen, and full of melancholic superfluities that come to various parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it occurs more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to them occasional purging with vinegar, and then heal the boil with balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron (i.e., a type of metal or instrument used for medical purposes) is in two ways: one is that they are cut off and then treated with fire the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you lift up the boil, and treat it all with fire.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision (or cut) is in this manner: first raise the leg with a hot iron very strong, so that the thick skin be softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch out the leg of the patient from above the knee down to the part under the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the boil in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a wide incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift out and treat with fire the black blood in your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up and command him that he eat strengthening foods with black vinegar.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume evacuation and treatment when the boils are empty and no longer harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The shaving of the leg is in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if it has much hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath and raise the leg with hot iron as long as it becomes red, and let the boils swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him up at the fire, and then cut off the place of the boil from the long part at the top of the kneecap, or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then dry the skin with a hot iron, and scrape out the boil from each side, as long as it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it looks red and black, and when it comes out through the skin it resembles a white string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then press the knife under it, as long as it is lifted up from the skin, and then let it dry with a light iron.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place above the three fingers, and then scrape out the skin over the boil until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then dry it with the iron, as you have done, and let it dry on another iron, just as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then dry it and cut it at the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then treat and dry it up to the second incision, then stretch from incision to incision until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot treat and dry it, then insert an awl into every strong double thread.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and treat it, and insert it under one of the threads, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, it cannot be treated or dried, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have treated it all, then put moist wool with vinegar and rosed oil on the wound site, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the flesh boil is contracted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you should split it crookedly, but do not cut it at all, and treat it in the way that we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the boil is curved, and does not sever completely, so as not to cut the boil.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a thick curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the boil, but be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	The common boil.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This boil is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land that has little moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it occurs on other parts than the legs, and this happens from the filth that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	such as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms, lodged between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this boil are that it comes to the leg with a very great inflammation.
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the boil begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the boil opens, it is necessary to wrap around it with a strip of linen from 1/2 to 3 fingers in length, and then bind it tight.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen stay on the leg, and every time it becomes loose, rewrap it around the linen and bind it tight again.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining part around, and do not cut it in its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and filth in that place, and a great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary to treat it little by little up to the top and leave nothing in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this boil when treated reaches a length of 5 palms or 10.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once an hour came to me, from which it emerged 10 palms in length, and when you cut it, it leaves a hole or a pit, and pierces down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and so everything comes out, and the matter inside is emptied out, and then administer to the place medicines that prevent filth from coming back for a day, and then treat it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this boil has many roots, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there come out many pits and from which it shoots roots; then treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "the disease of an ox", because it has occurred many times among cattle.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes all through the body, rising and falling.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt well as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it goes and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is lodged in filth from various humors, such as come worms and serpents and lice and ascarides or intestinal worms.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and we doubt its wickedness, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it gets in and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and treated, he can not be gotten rid of as long as it goes on:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong thread tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut up top and treat with fire, and if the worm is deeply in the flesh and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so cauterize it with fire above, until it burns.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does is that he corrupts the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see him coming close to the eye, then insert under it a thread in a loop shape, then cut up top and treat with fire.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient in purifying the body with soluble medicines for the corrupting humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and avoid foods that cause corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vacirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member, and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the boil of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and little by little, the boil rose just like a worm to the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, just like hot iron when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then little by little it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from member to member, because I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen that good people had moved pain from one place to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body and her boils were uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, the windiness constraint appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in those who are well-nourished, and have moist bodies and well-filled boils.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this illness being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up just as we have said.
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	so tie above and below hastily, and then cut up top until the constraining windiness bursts out from that place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it coming out yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with those things that expel the windiness, such as fetid pills and serpent's pills and similar others.
Des saiettes	The splinters.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, small ones, hairy, and glued (soudées) ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two edges, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are fragments (pieces).
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that falls in any member, it falls in two ways: either it falls into a principal member, or it falls into a secondary member.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so be careful with the extraction of this splinter, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this bad sign does not appear and the splinter is not deeply inside, then treat it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain, when the splinter falls there and pierces the bone, and causes a pus to burst out above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is blindness and deafness and convulsions and redness in oneself, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it comes out through the nostrils or ears, and perhaps it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and it bursts out from the moist white wound like pus, and also breaks through the flesh like an abscess of the body.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see these signs, be careful with the treatment, and extract the splinter if it is not in too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the splinter when it falls on the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the splinter moves like pus, and cuts black blood, and comes with cold sweat and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then be sure without a doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter that never leaves the spleen is that a foam bursts out from the wound and the throat swells up, and the patient's skin turns color, and they gasp high and cry for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter falls in the covering of the intestines, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great distress, and they gasp; and all the members from the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls in the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat bursts out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow sticks in the stomach and jumps into the intestine through a hole, then there is no hope for treatment nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow sticks in the bladder and urine jumps out and comes out through it, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and neck and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and forearm and elbow and knee and toes and the limbs similar to them, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, therefore do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to me, that is to say, at home of a friend with an arrow that fell in the arm in the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I attempted it, and I drew it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I saw a boy with an arrow that fell in the fat of the eye under the eyelid,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was wedged in and I could not pull out anything except the tip towards the fist.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was great like a Turkish bow, entirely of light iron without ears; the boy was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I saw an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I sawed off the fletching, and handled it so delicately that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I saw an arrow in a man, that it had fallen in his stomach, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then because he had passed 30 days, so it did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and sewed him up, and drew out the arrow, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man with an arrow that had fallen on his back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and it did not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, with an arrow that had fallen in his face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without great suffering pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I saw an arrow in the leg of a prince of the king, that it had fallen into the knee.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was entirely wedged in.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to the care after it had fallen 3 days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for an infection with a very fine thread, and did not feel any.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the place a plaster attractive and digestive, so that the place would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the place of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the same plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in that condition for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so much so that he felt the arrow one day inside his knee, and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicament of strong corrosive bile for several days, until it was completely open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I searched it, and felt the head of the arrow which had become inflamed at the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound that corrosive medicament until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed very well around the end for 4 months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then she opened up so much that I inserted the tongs in it, and pulled out the arrow from one side and the other, and could not get out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop searching and sewing with various instruments, until I took it out one day with well-made tongs.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, so that I drew it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can put your care on what I do not say, because books cannot contain everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters will gather and know a few important things, and those that are present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new work, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not get out of the limbs or where they are stuck except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered, or from the other side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out on the same side as it entered is a spear entering into fleshy parts, and does not jump out again immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out immediately, let it be left so that the flesh is corrupted around it, and the way out is made clear.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if she is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it be left so for some days, and moistened each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if not, make a small hole all around with a fine drill, until the surrounding flesh is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and any of the accidents that I have said happened to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it so for a few days, until it is equalized.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes just up to the surface of the skin, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself, and does not come out up to the surface of the skin,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for a few days without bad accidents, if he is sewn back together.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, administer tarers around it, as I have told you; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body and cannot be seen, search for it with every thread.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with any convenient instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein to hinder it, then break the skin as wide as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow to which it holds.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so take off the flesh that is stuck from two sides as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow itself, so that you may pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is corrupted, then pull it out, for the extraction will be made clear.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding becomes contrary, administer what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and use an instrument as you can to pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest aid it can be; and if you cannot, then put it back according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes out from the other side, either if it has pierced some part of it, or the skin is inflamed in the place where one can see or feel it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut up to, so that the tongs can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it jumps out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around gently, so that it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it again, and then resume the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the handle of the arrow is there, insert all the handle into it.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the handle slips out and you see that you must administer some kind of binding, then use a curved instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the curve of the instrument; and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is curved, insert a pointed instrument into its curve, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has penetrated deeply, it is fitting that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then care for the wound as befits.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is near to the spleen or to the belly or to the bladder or to the side, and you can cut up to it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then pull out the arrow, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and tiny, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the curved instrument is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push into the point of the arrow, as shown here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and knowing if it fits thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	arteries of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one bleeds are 31, of which there are 16 in the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two temporal veins that are behind the ears, which are called "artery of the temple".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "nasal arteries".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the back of the neck.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and they are called "angular veins".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins from which one bleeds commonly are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median one is called "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the scrotum.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that vein from which one bleeds, which appears clearly above the pubic area.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvatelle is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one of which is under the curve of the left thigh.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second superficial one that is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "Nesse" that is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins behind the ears is said to help against ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleeding, as I told you, is that you lift up the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two small depressions of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	search for them then with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, make a sign with your finger.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand in one motion all along the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and the vein well on both sides of the crossing point, and let the blood come out as much as you see fit.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind it up tightly, so that it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is said to be effective against ancient migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and against sore eyes, habitual conjunctivitis, and sharp pains in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bleeding is such as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient tightens their neck so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels for the pulse under their thumb, and makes a sign with their finger.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift up the skin over the vein upwards to your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you did in the other two veins, and let out blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger over the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of its cutting and extraction, in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is said to be just as effective as the bleeding of the cephalic vein against ancient facial diseases, and migraines, and jaundice.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient tightens their neck in a twist, so that the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fossor", whose shape is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the pointed end on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let out blood according to how much you see fit.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein tightly so that it is healed, and make sure to leave no mark from a burn wide.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the burns be too severe, and the bleeding cross over, because the bone is close by, and it's possible that the burn will break through when it becomes more subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the corners of the eyes is said to help against the eyes, and against jaundice, and against redness in the eye, and against facial diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck in twisting it from any point, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed, and let the bleeding of the crossing be about a finger's length long, but not too wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the burn becomes subtle, it may break through; then let out blood as much as you need, and then bind up with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein at the back of the neck is said to be effective against ague, and against severe sore throat, and against facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and jaundice that come in the face, and especially when they are ancient.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, then presses their back against your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the slender burn, and press it into the space between the two nostrils, right in the lip.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not appear well there, and the blood will now start to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not push too far inwards, and let out blood as much as you need, then bind it up for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the burn:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two jugular veins is said to help against swelling of the throat, and against choking, and against many diseases, and against congestion, and against corrosion, and against herpes, and inflammation.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck under both veins, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master should be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient should sit on a seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the vein deeply but not too widely, then draw out blood temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same in the other vein, then release the ligature, and bind the veins moderately around them.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangulated, and leave it until morning, when the wound will be healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips:
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips is said to help against sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and around the neck.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and tighten their neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip upwards, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left lip.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the tiny black veins surrounding them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut into both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below them, because it is the same procedure.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health under the tongue if it helps after the health of the head and this is at the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healer is that the patient sees between your hands in front of the sun, and raises their tongue, and looks under on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	heal then one and the other, and do not go too deep for there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the throat which we commonly heal are healed in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with one and the same fine olive-sized flame, or subtle olive-like flame as you hear cuttings, and it is called "anacel".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is very well known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to open the hairy veins full of thick blood that appears, and contain thick and murky blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer when pointed, and is for healing fine veins, or where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is suitable for the healer to heal slowly and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he strikes the artery, and a great deal of blood comes out, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not pierce with the flame, but cut like an acel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it is necessary to tie it and take out another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want to let go of it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and strike it with the flame acel, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the healing, then it is necessary that you tie up the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you recognize the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then tie up the arm, and strike the vein with the flame acel.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: flee from it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your thumb on high for a long time, then take it off if the bleeding has stopped, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	tie up the arm and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on high alert, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it bothers you, and the medicine is not present, then strike the artery if it opens, because its head recedes; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a skin of fig tree, dry it, and take one half and tie well to the other edge.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding stops, it's good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not mixed in more than one condition for the small size of the wound, and the power of the lien (a type of bandage) of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in the middle helps to treat bleeding from the head above and the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and the cephallix (a type of vein), as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is suitable for the healer to beware of the nerve that is underneath, and if he pierces too deeply and finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the healing is mixed, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you treat it with the instrument acel; and flee from the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, then cut them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the cephallix helps to treat bleeding from the head and also helps itself;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal with a piercing by olive oil flame or myrtle flame, for it is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not harm anything if we fail the first time, and then try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and it may happen that the places swell in some people when we fail the first time, but they do not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know for healing, is that healing is not accomplished except by preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off illnesses from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and that the healing is done in one of the three ways which are hot or cold: to wit, cephalic, phlegmatic, and sanguine;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should heal oneself at the beginning of spring and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should heal oneself on the first day or the third after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing which is administered against illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not suitable to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying more than the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should old people who have passed 60 years be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner it may be, they should cleanse the intestines with a light purgative.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if it has many impurities retained, so that the vessels may not attract the unnecessary superfluities which are harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal oneself who is too fat with meats, nor drunk until they are sober, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should not be healed after a great passion of colic, and vomiting, and disturbance of the belly, and multiplication of urinating with women, and travail, watching, and toil, and all that is done by virtue or something from arms or from body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then temper the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and by medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then bathe or take a bath, if nothing else hinders, to temper the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal yourself from the venom of the belly around the third day, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be joyful and happy, and the healer should be higher than he who is being healed, and gently wipe his arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the bandage on top slowly, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot cure the blood.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then gently rub the area with your hands, until the veins swell and are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	and then moisten the healer's hand with the flame of a flask of old oil, then put their thumb on top of the swelling area under the skin where they want to heal.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the swelling does not burst or break when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are swellings that burst like cords to be cut by the healer, and those of such nature as are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the flame on it, it recoils from the flame, and cannot open up the swelling, and thus is of those things.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts open, the wound is too narrow, because of this, it's necessary for the healer to be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts open the first time, it's good; but if not, then he should repeat it again a little below or above that same spot quickly, unless the place is still swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the patient fears, then he should leave it for one or two days and not bind the arm again.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come pus-filled boils; don't take a bath until then, and if it pleases him, he should repeat the healing again.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the puncture is small or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it's not as much blood as you see, then stick the flame directly into the same puncture.
