et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it will work a little quickly, so that the place becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not repeat the healing again, and put a little of linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is more suitable in this place than the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil in each healing that you perform for swellings, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done with lard and goose fat, when it is put on the place; it tempers the blood and breaks apart when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess which often happens, just the same as when it is not healed quickly enough or the opening of the swelling is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten and put on the place a wet sponge in hot water and vinegar for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the swelling, and if there remains a blackness or greenish color at the place after some days, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see fit, put on something made of aloe or myrrh reconstituted in vinegar, mustard juice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there comes an abscess and appearance of illness at the site of the healing from the basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be cautious not to put on anything from what we have said, for perhaps the blood will flow from an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each type of blood according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Since the joint is black, let it come out until it is red; and if you see a vein large, let it go until it becomes fine; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is suitable for one who is swollen and bruised, and needs bloodletting, to make the wound larger, and have the flaps wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it needs to be healed quickly and often, and it should be healed by cutting across, not by puncturing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of healing is safe from bleeding and cutting nerves, and is more valuable than a long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body is failing from the wound, it is necessary to give wet bread in juice of quinces; if he is overheated, let him take blood three times or four.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he has a cold complexion, give him wet bread with honey syrup before the surgery; or with aromatic honey and spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he falters at the surgery, after the flow of blood stops, it is necessary that he smells broth of meat and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have said in the chapter on fainting, for evacuation of bad blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to evacuate his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great surgery, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to evacuate his arm after the first surgery, and he has a strong body, should heal in 7 hours after the first surgery, or after the 9th hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed from another side, should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood inside the body that is already heated and brings fever; it is necessary to draw a large quantity and to enlarge the wound as much as possible until he reaches a calm state.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Now that you've explained all the healing conditions, and put your hand on his pulse when he heals, so that death does not come in place of peace.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens often when the surgeon is careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it's not a good idea to let go of the arm and have bleeding occur again, and the wound is closed, when you press down firmly on top;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	or if it's crooked, let him stretch out his arm quickly, because that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him alone until he heals again; or if you can't sew with the thread at the flame tip, so long as the blood which has congealed is still at the edge of the wound.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on I.e. a pot of thread that has been soaked in water, and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, let it be alone and do not bind it tight until the inflammation has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let blood again the second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another wound, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The wound on the arm is healed in that place instead of the wound of the head because it is complicated.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the scab is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately so that the wound appears well, then let it heal from end to end, neither wide nor long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if the wound is wide and heals well near the joint of the hand, and there's no more bleeding, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's winter, don't put your hand in hot water again, because you would put it more in heat than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this wound is safer from all other wounds, there being no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salvetelle (a type of blister) on the right hand is worth more than all liver diseases, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and soak it in hot water, until the swelling is gone, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it heals across, and you cover it all over with a bandage, then nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too deep, for the nerves are under the skin, naked of fat,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as it's necessary for you to let, then put on the swelling oil and bandage to bind quickly, and thus do with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The swelling on the left hand is worth the sickness of the gout, and do with it just as I told you to do with the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The swelling on the shoulder is worth all the diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as gout, retention of urine, disease of the reins, and old knees and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his swelling is that the sick person puts their foot in hot water and rubs on the swelling until it is gone.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and they put something over the joint of the foot; and if the swelling is at the ankle, and there are many swellings on top of the foot,
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heave out then the most swollen place, or at the ankle, that weighs most.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have taken out the swelling on top of the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and let it heal in the same way as when it is cut; and let the flesh become again normal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood can't come out, then put the foot back in the water and let it bleed well out of the swelling.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the abscess bursts the first time, then start again the second time a little higher up, because the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear of nerve, as we have said, and do in the same way with the swelling on the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic swelling is at the knee of the back leg, and its abscess is worth the pain in the back when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its abscess is that the sick person goes to bathe and rubs on top of the knee with four fingers in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the swelling will not burst open; and if it bursts, then let it drain in all ways that you can, and crosswise.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth as much as if you had cut it open, because the place is very salty, and it is often returned to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find the cause, then let out a vein from it that bursts on the back of the foot and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much to stop the bleeding that you see, then untie the ligature and put on a compress and tie it tightly; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	A new section!
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and bloodletting is done in two ways: either by piercing to attract blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this bloodletting which is done without piercing is in two ways: either it is hot-blooded, or not hot.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and bloodletting which is done by piercing and drawing out blood is done in 14 parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	one is on the soles of the head; and the others are on the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on each side of the neck; and the leech under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the leeches on the shoulders; and the leech above the kidneys.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the leeches in the two arms; and the leeches on the two legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches on the two ankles; and bloodletting does not draw out blood, but only small vessels that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it is not as feeble as venesection of a vessel.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable that it be administered, neither hot nor cold, in any illness that comes from excess, until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to bleed because of illness or by habit, let us administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness in themselves.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and are reaching for blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who dream, and see with their mind's eye blood and wounds and bites and seeming things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is in the middle of the month, let us command that they be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the nose is helpful for the pain of the head... that comes from themselves, and it's not suitable that this be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bloodletting is in place of bleeding from the brain.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it's not suitable for those who have a cold complexion to bleed, or who are constipated, because this does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it's not suitable for the elderly to bleed, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves, become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping glass should be placed a little lower on account of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The bloodletting in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the brain, and for this reason it is suitable for tightness of the chest.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for rupture of the channel of the womb, and for wind, and for excess.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be placed a little deeper, because if it is too tightly held, it provokes forgetfulness or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The bloodlettings on the two sides of the neck are worth for headaches, and eye pain, and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of bleeding from the brain; and let you command the bleeder that he stretch his hand to take, that he not strike the artery, and that he come back with decorum of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The bloodlettings under the chin are worth for illnesses of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of bleeding from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bloodlettings on the shoulders are worth for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The bloodlettings in the arms are worth as much as those of the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the bleeder that he not go too deeply in, because the place is bare of flesh, and lies on nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is above the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it's necessary that the cupping glass be large, and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and if it were subtle, it would break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs are quite effective, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are worth for old pains in the groin, and in the loins, and in the bladder, and help to dissipate the swelling; and they take the place of two saphena veins, and two ankles, but however, they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and then suck immediately, and place it hastily, and move equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the blood appears redder; then remove, and put the cupping glasses back, and take care of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores: so it's necessary to hit only once, and it's necessary to make large cuts, and a little deep ones, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to hit twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the sinew is very thick, then you must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out some blood little by little, it suffices to do this once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to draw out much blood, then we recommence often; and if the sinew is thick, then strike it in depth, and the ends should be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is advisable to that one who has thick skin and hard, and who have broad pores, that you anoint the sites of the cupping glasses with perfumative and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in esteem, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in vinegar, of onion oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or of balm, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And to him in whom one treats a soft flesh and wide pores, it is not advisable to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is advisable to wash afterward with rosewater, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or pearl water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise with ass's milk, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of juniper, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable to treat with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath, and should not sleep after the treatment.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is advisable that he be warned, both when he must be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are sick with a choleric temperament, and if their blood is too thick and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it's necessary that he take cold things, such as grapes and turnips and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young pork, and kid goat meat, and moistened meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, if they take honey syrup, and medium wine that is between old and new, and young pork, and young pigs, and small game birds and partridges.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will sweat, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it's necessary to give certain men some time three-legged or masticated before the sweating, or after, in order to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and temper the blood, but it's not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The plasters that are put without hurting the skin are those that are placed over the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the flank, for these members cannot bear to be hurt there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done so that blood can be drawn from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the shoulders when the night dew seeps in; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as when we put plasters on the belly and on the navel to reduce the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is swelling or bruising, and by its attractive virtue it sometimes draws out the swelling, or dislodges the splinter from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so it does when it is put on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind or gas.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these plasters are administered empty to suck only that much, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times filled with warm wine.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in eye diseases, and in such a way that the plaster is filled with hot water alone, or with water that has been cooked with herbs that are beneficial to it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the plaster administered on fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 thumbs in width and half a palm in depth, and on the edge around the middle there is one small notch, such as to stick a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be of lead, soft in front so that it does not hurt the patient when put on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and it has in its middle a rod from side to side of lead or iron, so that a candle can be enclosed.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there should be both big and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the plasters for children are different from those for old people, and for thin ones than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one should put this plaster on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	put the candle with wax or a small linen in it, and put it inside the plaster across the rod that is inside the plaster.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light be at the bottom of the plaster so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and you should have a small cloth over the notch that we said to be placed there, so that when one wants to go, the vapors will rise, and take off the plaster.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and then put on a new linen cloth, just like before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore, the plaster administered for eye disease has no rod or notch at all, and is only used when it is filled with water, and is put on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and that's its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	without a rod are only used when it is not possible to put plasters on their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare places of flesh, such as the elbow or knee, and other similar ones.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of this user is that when you find plasters that are in sweet clear waters without sediment, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a new vessel filled with sweet clear water, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then it is to be soaked with wine and plaster, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the plasters.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and swollen, if it is a place where one can put a plaster, then put one on, for this helps much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, take off the poultice of ash and then of water, very well, and then squeeze it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too quickly on top of the plasters, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the plaster is hardened.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the ulcer is multiple, put on vinegar that has been crushed, or gallstones, and similar things, until it is hardened.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place half-cooked split peas, and leave them until they are dried to the ulcer, which will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other plasters.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the plasters do not stick well, rub the place with fresh blood, and then insert a needle until the plaster sticks.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are dried out, sprinkle on a small amount of burnt alum and silk ashes, or of ash, so that they will now dry even further.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds (or "The Book of Bruises").
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for wounds and swellings.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen, dear son, that the foolish man rejects this chapter, which was never seen in any of the old books, nor read from a letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is estranged the science in our land, for I have never found anyone good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing more, except through the science of old books, which I have studied so much and treated as such, and by experience, and through the habituation of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have shown you in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So then it is fitting that we say the prologue of this book, which are the summaries of words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven wise may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a wound or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient with all speed, and if nothing else fails, as weakness of body, or fever, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the patient's blood is too cold or too hot; and particularly in cases of coldness of the joints, and flesh of bird and goat, and does not drink wine, nor eats any greasy foods, and does not fill himself too much with meats that fill the vessels with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot aposteme or spreading of matter to the member; then return the patient to their first natural government as they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and peas, and veal, and oysters, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the flesh is repaired more quickly and the wound heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well repaired or united according to their natural condition due to the decay of the members, nor those who are too soft, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, rub on the broken bone thick compresses that are dried and join the member together, so that it becomes strong again as it was before; and do not take away its work, and because of this it needs to be nourished with thick meats, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that wounds are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the wound of the head is one thing, and the wound of the back or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of wounds.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are wounds that go around an arm or leg, and others that cut into it, such as the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also wounds with an open gash, and wounds with a small slit or tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own cure and proper instrument in restoration, according to the nature of the wound that comes to it.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and a bruise of the bone is known by this: that the place is twisted and open quite well on the outside, and sounds to the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or crunching sound, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no bruise.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have a crack, or split, or small bruise.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So do not move the hand, but put on medicines that come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the wound which goes around an arm or leg and causes the two parts to separate, it is necessary now to join them together equally, so that hot apostems do not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot apostems come, let it be left untouched for a day, until the apostem is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it back together equally to the original state that you can do lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of the bone is more lightweight than the restorations of one who has splintered pieces; then bind it, as is necessary later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is two parts, then whether it is your hand or foot, or at hand it is small members, or with two strings, or with one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are stretched out, you rub with all sorts of instruments the additions in their places to the point where you can, and take care that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join together well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the touch if you think it is not quite right: straighten it well, and do not bind it too tightly, or press it as those who bring heat and constriction to the member by their work, as we have said many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in its proper place, chastise the patient so that they do not move it, either while awake or asleep, whether walking or in another way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not in its proper place, and it needs to be put in such a condition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straight, so that twisting does not occur when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones, which need to be enveloped with soft and subtle linen wraps.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: they need to be enveloped with a wide and sturdy linen, because the wider linens enclose the entire large member and bind it evenly from all sides, so that there is no crease.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie the ends of the wraps lightly, three or four turns according to the member, and bind your hand with a little bit on all the linen, then go above the break and bind it less tightly than the break, so that the break is slightly apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen a little bit and a little bit more, until you take up a great part of the healthy skin, then take another linen and wrap it around again on the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first layer above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the wraps of linen or cloth, as long as it is all even, then tie everything up with one bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no swelling or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	and if there is swelling or apostem, then put on something that calms the hot apostem and removes the swelling, and let it be like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind the splints above with a piece of linen or wood of the same thickness as a well-made cane, or with a branch of palm tree, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the break is a little bit thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is needed for the member of smallness or greatness.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on top of the splints in the same way that you did at the first layer, then tie on top with a thread evenly, as we have said in the first layer above the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is on top, the looser; and it should be that the thread is moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, such as those works of fools who make their knots with twisted linen cords, and it is a great error, because the knot cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it should not have between each splint less than two threads' width.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the splints' ends after being bound in their healthy places, then put under them linen wrappings or torn flannel, so that they do not become worse.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the skin is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to bind with splints all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it does not need to put strong splints until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your security from hot apostem happening.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the ancient way of ointments to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: which is that you take flour that is kept at the mill walls, and mix it with abundance of egg, and put this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the restorative ointment for the break in many conditions, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of ointment that restores breaks, dislocations, and twists: take 3 parts of alum, laudanum, and galena, and gum arabic and myrrh, ana 20 parts; myrrh and aloes, ana 5 parts; and aloe, 9 parts. And make them into powder, and mix with abundance of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this ointment, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of ointment that is worth for twists: take myrrh and vellum, ana 20 parts; myrrh and aloes, ana 9 parts; acacia wood, 6 parts; Armenian balm, 10 parts. And grind them well, and mix with water or abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of ointment for joints and bones that are split from their places, and calms the pain occurring, and is used by those who suffer from a cut or break: take new linen, and moisten it in olive oil and cooked fat, and put on the place. This ointment does not restore, but it is good to calm hot apostem and properly remove pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and wild ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of ointment for the restoration of bone break and to soften the remaining apostem. Take root of vellum, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is hot, mix with moisted water of coriander or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way of ointment even stronger than the first one, when hard apostem comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of vellum, and seeds of flax, balaustine, melilotus, and sanicola, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says that for the restoration of a broken member, one should only use a wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that for the restoration of a broken member, one should put on things which are slightly hot and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of ointment that is worth for lesion and pain: take myrrh and crushed horn of a wild goat, or bird's quill, and vellum, in equal parts, and grind them, and make an ointment with it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove the bandage a little while later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone shifted from its place; if it is so, do not remove the bandage for at least a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or swelling, with rest or inflammation, then hurry and remove the bandage, and take off the ointment now; and take a light cloth and sea sponge moistened in water, and plunge it into the water, and lift up the place, until the itching ceases and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then apply a warm compress, moistened with vinegar or rose oil, and bind on a cloth, until you are sure of hot swelling.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation in the member settle, and be freed of pain, then resume the subtle binding, and a small poultice, and do not strain it so hard as before; and bind subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the swelling is gone, and redness and pain and inflammation have ceased entirely, and you need to apply a poultice and binding again, so do it again, as you did first treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, do not remove the binding until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what is seen, until the bruise has faded, and the union approaches the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then the swelling will be more than before, and the flesh will become thicker, as I said before; and if you see that the area is drying out too quickly, know that suppuration cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	loosen the binding then with hot water soap, every time you remove it, and do so every other day, and rinse a little the bandage.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work the suppuration will be cut to the member, and quickly heal what foolish people, who left the member in a bad way, have done: it is wrong, and is fearful work, and I see nothing else but to lance and work properly. (Note: "lancer" means to lance or pierce something, as with a medical instrument)
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like the text has switched to a new topic. The phrase "des diverses manieres de brisure" can be translated to "of various types of bruising". This could be referring to different ways that people can experience bruising, or perhaps different methods for treating or describing bruises. If you'd like to share more context or continue with the translation, I'd be happy to help!
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of bruising and various forms, and their causes are determined; (lit. "determined" in the sense of being known or understood). This suggests that the text is going to describe different types of bruises, their appearances, and the reasons why they occur.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are bruises that are caused by the blow of a sword, and the elbow breaks all the bone just up to the spongy part that is underneath the bone, as if it had been struck by a hatchet or an axe; and because of this it is called this manner of bruising "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of bruising "absolute"; and the wound of these two bruises is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a fissure, or a bruise from a stone, or falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a bruise pressing, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has healed into the bone as subtle as an onion, and the fissure is small, and because of this it is called this bruise "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is made or by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone downwards, and it leaves a hollow such as blacksmiths make when they pour water onto the cauldrons; if it enters into the stone.

et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens in all these kinds of bruises where small fragments are torn off like this one, and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of bruises by the swelling on them, and the inflammation that has been tested, and by the corrupt flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary bruise is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and you rub your finger on it, if the bruise opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the bruise, be careful about the accidents that have befallen the patient. And if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of understanding, extension, palpitation, high fever, and the eyes coming out and becoming red, and other similar signs in more serious dispositions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the 14th day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the flesh under the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents which we have spoken of come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone bruise comes right up to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut into the damaged part thus: and this means that you take hold of the patient's head, wounded, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more carefully than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the discharging of pus comes to uncover the bone, or an ulcerous abscess appears, then with the help of those things which are needed, and this means that you fill the place with a cloth moistened in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	It seems that the text is describing a surgical procedure for treating a bone wound.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert a second swelling, one greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different swellings, some thick and others wide, and are pointed, and of iron hardness; and work on them lightly, lest you lacerate the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, it should be pierced around it, so that you can apply swellings with awls, but not so deep as for them to penetrate through the bone of the skull; and there should be above the point a border or a circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several of these, each coming into its place on the edge of the bone, so that you will have awls for all sides; and this is the shape of the three manners of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl on the bone, and turn it back and forth with your hands until you know the bone has been pierced; then put the awl in another place a little later, and do all around like this, and cut with the pincers the space of the bone which is between the piercings, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or with any of the tools you have such as tongs, forceps; and be sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to remove the shavings that remain of the bone from all the other tools resembling a pincer, but it should be more pointed and finer than the other pincer.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, then gently scrape them out with one of the tools; and then care for the wound with tents and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of working is what Galen says, which is more safe; and he affirms it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break shows clearly; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place beneath the head of this incisional lens the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you lightly chisel the bone all around, and be careful of the tissue that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, then lightly scrape it away, for one scrapes well without any harm or pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce all the way to the tissue, and the bone is chiseled only so far that it leaves small pieces, then you should cover over that roughness and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in various quantities, in order to smooth out each part as well as possible, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you go before large rasps and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and subtle breaks, you should smooth them out according to their direction. And it is a thing that cannot be easily mastered by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, you should take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled linen cloth, in two or three layers, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you don't irritate the flesh, then apply above another string, but not so tight that it only covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it stay for one or two days, until the swelling of the abscess is calmed down, then loosen it and apply medicines such as lily roots, flax flour, incense powder, aristolochic powder, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer gentle medicines without cauterization.

Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that never are the two bones of the nose broken at once, or one by itself alone, for they are two separate bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes dislocated or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should use your little finger or a probe from the nose, and insert it into that break in the nasal bone, and push it forward, so that the nose returns to its natural shape.

And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and you cannot reach it with your little finger, then you should put it back into place with a wooden mallet, not too big.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in both parts, then you should do it again, and hurry to restore the nose on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not on the first day, then after seven or ten days, when the swelling has gone down, you should place a cloth of linen at the head of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should place another cloth on the other part, if the break is there; and let the tents be so big that they fill the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. And the doctors said that you should moisten the tents with butter and change them every day. It doesn't seem right to me, but it's necessary that they be moistened with a mixture of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent in place until the bone is hard and the cartilage has become firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time should you place an egg poultice in the nose instead of a tent, and if you have a soft cloth available, wrap it around and keep the breakage together, and breathe through the patient's nose. Do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerote or moistened cotton in rose oil or a small pouch of diachylon into the nostril.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if swelling does not come to the nostril, put an ointment on the outside, made from wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light bandages over it, and do not bind the nose too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break in the nose is small and it has broken into tiny pieces, then you will draw them out with instruments suitable for this case, then sew up the wound, and treat it with things that prevent gangrene and promote healing, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this case.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put poultices on it until he is cured.
