de la routure de la mandibule	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is out of place, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is so slight that only, and not at all broken in two, forward than bent inward, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side of the mandible, then put your index finger from the right hand and push the fracture inward lightly, and fasten it to the other hand by outward, and make sure.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of 2 inches by 3 inches until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the dislodging of the teeth has happened, or bruising, then stretch threads from gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken mandible ointment, and put on one double cloth; and on the cloth a well-made great bandage, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it up at your discretion that you can, and command the patient to rest, and give them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's condition is changing, then unbind on the third day, and then reapply what has been changed; and put plaster on it, of mill powder with abundant egg or flaxseed flour, after having removed the ointment; and put on a light linen bandage. If the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as is until they are healed; many times people heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil or abscess appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, remove the loose bone fragment from it; use subtle tools suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, sew up the wound if it is large, and put on one suitable ointment to prevent scarring, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade breaks more than once in front of the shoulder, and the break is in three manners: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without a wound, you have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder blade which is broken; and the other extend the neck towards the part; then place the break in your arms, so that the form be as it should be, and there is no appearance or bending.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded rod of cloth or linen, and make it as large as needed; then stretch and lift the shoulder blade, and hold the rod in your hand, so that you can put the break back into its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder blade out to the front because it is too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies on their back and places a middle bolster under their shoulder; then push the assistant down on the shoulder so that the bone of the shoulder blade is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your arms, and if you find it disjointed, it is necessary that you split it open; and pull out the fragments lightly, and if the bone cannot join together with any adjustment, cut it at one of the incisors that you have; but make sure to place this instrument under the shoulder blade so as to hold it in its proper position.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and shape it like a spoon, and do not bend it, and make it as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and have two handles, just as you see, one wide and the other narrow, so that they match the contours of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure that the wound is hot and inflamed, it is necessary to cauterize it; and if the laceration is small or you doubt that it is hot, you should apply a poultice of linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot inflammation comes, you should soak a piece of linen in rose oil, garlic, and wine, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The immobilization of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you place on the bone a poultice made of flour and egg whites, and put light bandages over it, and place a rod under the shoulder, if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage of an arm's length in width, then place a double-layered linen cloth over it and the poultice; then take a slender strip of three fingers' breadth in width and length, and envelop it around that bandaged part, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And place the strip over the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the ailing one; and wash each part, and when you see that the dressing holds the break firmly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then leave it as it is every day; and when the stitches loosen, restrain them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And make the patient lie on their back, and have them place a small bolster under the healthy shoulder, so that they can lift the assistant up; this will help to reduce the break of the collarbone by aligning the shoulder blade, or when you bind the arm to the neck. And do not untie it, unless bad events come to pass within 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And then restart the dressing, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it so, until they are restored; and they are usually restored within 28 days, and in some cases less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Whenever the shoulder breaks or leaves its place and can only be felt by touch; if it heals according to the shape of the break, and is reset according to its natural form in all ways you can, then dust the area with miller's flour with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top. Then put on a large and subtle pad, one peg bigger than the shoulder, and under the pad are threads in any place of the shoulder, so that those threads from linen bandages tie it evenly; and then bind everything with a strong strip, so that the pad does not move from its place, and inspect the bond each day; and every time it loosens, tighten it again, and put the patient on their side, and the shoulder is reset in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, loosen it and be sure, because it's not the bone that will come out easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone sticks out and points under the skin, then take it up and draw it out, and do what we have said to calm an abscess or hot swelling.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que vous avez mentionné un autre type de blessure, celle du "pis" (probablement le poitrail ou le bassin).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken inside, then it descends below, and the patient feels great pain, and is unable to straighten it, and quickly, and by chance may vomit blood, and reveal the splintered bone in the bone that was broken, and he senses well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back, and they place .i. (one) cushion between their shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join the ribs of .ij. (two) ribs with their hands, and carefully try to put it together in every way you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply ointments and bandages on top of the staff made of salt or other light wood, and wrap it around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the strap back behind, and tighten it slightly, and release each hour a little, and if it swells, then tighten it; and if it seems convenient to unfasten, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and clean the ointment, and address what has come from ways of cures; then rinse the ointment, and tie it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	C'est l'objet du texte que nous avions ! Le titre semble être une référence à un manuscrit médiéval qui traite de la fracture des côtes.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come but in the thick places after the back, and to the head inside, and do not bend but because they are slippery; and one senses well at the examination of the shoulders.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the remedy is that you put the splinter back in place just like it should be. And then put a poultice on it, and a bandage made of an iron rod, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is sloping inward, then the patient feels very great pain and pricking, as well as a feeling like pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane; and he laments with sharp pains, and chokes and vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and in the past they have used great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods which inflate the belly, so as to push the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses form there, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And among us, one said that you should put cups on the place to suck out strongly, and it seems like a good reason; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract the superfluities to the place because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And among us, one said that you should cover the place with wet wool soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to put the linen back in its place, then treat it as if it were a case of pleurisy, meat wound, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain from the bone that punctures the membrane and is in doubt, it seems necessary to split open above the place of the broken rib, and then put an instrument underneath to protect the surrounding tissue; and then one should cut through the bone, and remove it lightly, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is healed. And if abscesses come, one should place wet cloths soaked in rose oil on top of them on the place; and treat the place as for an abscess, and be cautious that the rib stays in its proper place, so to speak, as long as it takes to heal.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a breakage comes to the bones of the neck, and it breaks, causing the person to bend down; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be saved or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that they are mortal in many dispositions, and if they can move them and feel well when one holds them back and pricks them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care into it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will be saved or not, take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in hands, and on top of the back there is windiness and vomiting without will, and when one has placed it on their stomach, there is windiness and vomiting without will. And when it is placed on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: if it does not work at all in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you put something on it if there is an hot abscess, if you put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is calmed down; then put a comforting and drying poultice on it and tie it with a cloth, and command the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone breaks loose, it is necessary to cover the wound with a cloth; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a suture, then heal the wound with ointment dripping with fat, until it is cured. And if the splinter of the bone is broken, which is called "the splinter of the cow", put your fist from your left hand into it and place it equal to the other hand in your power, then put the poultice and bandage on it, if you need them; then tighten it, and if there are loose bones, make a splint on it, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here's a rough translation:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	A small diminishment occurs in the head when the bones of the back are broken; and if it happens, then there is not much reduction in height; and they become two long ones, and decline towards each other, and come to the patient with pain at the place, and a puncture, and inflammation where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above it, as much as the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is only in the head alone, then put this same breakage back in its natural place.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is long, or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, as much as the restoration of this breakage will become apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, then apply the splint, and then apply a wedge of wood or of horn, and bind the breakage so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs, as much as the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and apply what we have said before that; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as it should be, if no bad accident occurs; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	La brisure de l'ajutoire (ou de la cuisse)
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those who are between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one straight branch from a green twig, larger in size.
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the branch together with two pieces of string, and let it hang down, and have the patient sit on one seat; then throw the broken arm above the branch so that it comes into place, and has a wooden curve in the middle; then make the patient hang from any heavy thing or the servants stretch it downwards; then place the physician's hands equally on the fracture, until the break returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one straps the patient on their bed, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two servants to have one pull what is above the fracture to his hands, and the other to pull from below all the strings, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the traction is too strong, then tighten one string below and above the fracture, and stretch each servant to their part. And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it's necessary that you put a medium string underneath the seat, and another towards the collarbone, under the fracture; and similarly if the break is towards the collarbone, it's necessary to put one string lightly without effort, so that the break is equal above the bone, and above the collarbone; then put the break back together as needed, and strain it, but if there are abscesses, don't.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, then don't strain it at all for seven days, and put a warm compress on linen oil on the arm and shoulder, until the abscess is calmed down; then strain it, and the way to strain it is that you put the splint above the fracture, then assemble the arm with a support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the cloth, and strain above the support, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, if no other thing prevents it, or if the bone has not been moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone has not been moved, use splints, and place above the fracture a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two inches between each one, and have each splint be so large that it passes over the break three inches from each side; then strain on the splints, in such a way as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, stronger and less distanced.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the shape of the splints and the straining, as we have said, to restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, then let it be tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check each three days the bandage, that it does not become purulent or inflamed at the site, or that swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. If so, adjust, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not untie it until three days or more have passed, and the patient should sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place underneath the support one cushion full of wool evenly, and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not change, or that the bandage becomes soft. If it is adjusted by the virtue of medicine, then give them food in the manner we previously mentioned, so that the food is at the first subtleties; and when they begin to recover, it should be substantial.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one small and one large, with the small one at the shoulder and the large one below it; by chance, you may break either the small or the large bone alone, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the treatment is easy and the recovery; and when the large one is broken, it has a bad and more grievous recovery than when both are together broken. If only the small bone is broken, then you must gently extend the arm and put it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then you must stretch it more strongly; and have him lie on one pillow, and turn his hand higher than the others, and his small bones lower than the others, and he himself should be crossed over him, and a pillow in front of him higher than the patient so that the patient suffers no pain; then stretch out another servant's arm to the part under his hand, or to one string, and another servant to another above. And then put the mirror even with his better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then put each one back in its place, and if any is dislocated that you can't restore it to its place, then send for a surgeon, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I've spoken about it in the chapter on singular wounds; then take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the treatment a foul-smelling suppurative swelling occurs, then apply a cloth made from rose oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft; and tie the cloth gently over it, so that the swelling is calmed. And then remove the cloth and put on an ointment made with flour powder and plenty of egg yolk; apply the stars, and make sure that the star for the break is stronger and slightly larger than the others. And know that there should be 6 or more stars in various positions: either the break is in one bone, or in two; and stretch the bandage more tightly over the break than elsewhere, always lessening it as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and the cloths above the break should be soft and moist, not hard or harsh; and the threads from which it is stretched should be made of linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the limb after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, you should bathe the member in hot water until the itch is calmed; and do not let the member rest too tightly. And then resume the bandaging, and if the ligament is softened and the bone is dislocated, and appears to be so, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you should moisten it with one pess (i.e., a poultice) and let it be for some days until the swelling flows into it, and then tie.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not untie it until twenty days or thereabouts, and then let him lift his hands to his neck, and may his necks be equal, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and in its arm there occur many kinds of breaks, and it comes to be creased or bent many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the wrist of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cross their legs and sit straight in front of them equally; then put their hand on the stretched sheet, and stretch out the splints over the broken bones, and place them even with the mirror, so long as they are well joined together; and apply the plaster and bandages, if swelling comes, then put an iron band according to the size of the wrist; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the side of the wrist near the stomach, make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to squeeze it against their broken wrist; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the iron band be as soft as possible, but also large enough for the wrist, and bind it in the same way.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, it is necessary that you put an iron band on top and another underneath in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the bones of the wrist, and it is the thumb, then put them equal, as is necessary; and bind with the wrist, and if you see that you should put a small straight iron band to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in another bone, such as the index or one of the others, then put them equal, and tie with the healthy bone that is behind; or tie them all together in one holding, which is worth something, or put a splint on top, as you would for a thumb; and take care of the restoration and the disposition of the swelling that comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons terminé la lecture de ce texte médical ancien. Voulez-vous continuer avec une autre partie du texte ? Ou bien est-ce pour une raison spécifique que vous avez mentionné "de la cuixe brisie" ?
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	Il semble que nous ayons repris le texte médical ancien.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each limb to its equal part; and this is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is close to the root of the thigh, so that one of the limbs is towards the elbow, and the other limbs are below the breakage. And also if it is close to the knee, then so the limb is near the knee, and the extension is downward; then place the splint on the bone in equal parts with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if there are abscesses that come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, so let it subside then return to your work and care for the patient; the bandaging is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap over the breakage one strong doubled band in three or four turns, and leave the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and let the end of the thread come up; then turn over the leg and over the thigh the band, then put on top of the breakage splints, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then wrap the loose ends between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to put equal pressure, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns on the breakage; and as you go up from the breakage, so is the pressure less; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return to below at the end of the thread, until you come near the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, lest there come a swelling or abscess or other similar appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it swells, so let it be untied and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, so it is necessary to remove them if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area, and extract whatever can be extracted; and then cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never once is the thigh broken in such a way that one puts splints on it, as on the arm or leg; nevertheless, in this kind of treatment the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little more or less, according to the various constitutions of the patients.
de la ruelle dou genoil	De la rupture du genou.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there is sometimes a break, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, then it's only a fissure, or i.e. a perforation, and causes all pain, and without pain, and this seems good to everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus: you put back what was broken to its place, so that it can move again as much as possible; then apply an ointment, and if necessary, insert a rounded wooden splint, and bind it as needed, then re-align all the dislocations which we have mentioned in other fractures, such as warm compresses and similar treatments. Then apply to each accident what is fitting for it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of a break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg are two bones, of which one is called by right "tibia" and the other is called "fibula"; and it has all another break as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is thus equal to that of the arm also, and the operation is entirely the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns out in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the thick bone (tibia) is broken, it feels like great pain and it's easily seen, and it turns under. Then apply an extension, and put it back together, and bind the splints equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be minor and more lightweight; and make it as gentle as your virtue permits.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your operation, take two wooden splints that cover the leg from one end to the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them in two layers of bandages, one on top and one on the bottom, and bind them together in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some administer a wooden bar of the length of the leg, and made of wood, and put the leg in it to prevent movement, and properly clean the wound in the break; and move each day the leg, to see if there is warm swelling or another accident; and treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of a break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle rarely breaks, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and crush, and there is no other injury than bruising in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the sick foot on the earth, just like it would go, and then put your own foot on top of it, where the bones are raised, and press down so that they return to their proper place; then apply the splint and bandage above, and under the foot of the hurt foot a small board with two grooves, then tie it firmly to the foot with string or thread, then wrap cloth around, and other things which you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equalized, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put a splint on the broken toe, according to the length of the toe, and make it a little wider, then place under the foot that board which I mentioned, and tie it firmly in place; and if there are two or three or more toes broken, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and tie the board under the foot securely; and have the end of the board projecting out from the foot, so that it is well fastened.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, as we have discussed; and treat each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a break of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the wrist of a woman is broken, then she should sit with her arm extended, and be inclined towards the back part, and held from behind; then fill the natural hole of the wrist with cotton, and put in as much as one fist; then let the woman stand up and lift her hand little by little, and thus the cotton will come out to the entrance of the natural hole, and the bone will return to its place along with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, put it back in, and do this for about 7 days or so: then the break will be restored. If you want to see, take a bladder of a goat, and tie a cord around the anus, and fill the entire bladder with air; then blow into the cord forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside: the natural hole will return to its normal place, and thus restore the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or a woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the hip; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into this book and listens to my words. For the break signifies the right path of restoration in many dispositions: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or so: and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or arm or similar, that he be healed immediately, so that the stitches which we have said may witness to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and an abscess forms, then close it with pitch, or if you have nothing else, then start to restore the break in that very same hour or day, so that pus does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes out, then let the restoration alone for just nine days, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the tenth day or the quarter, because you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin's surface, it is necessary that you gently point it out with your fingers, making a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put on level with your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 prongs of length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the doctor that he takes 3 or 4, as needed in each cure of break; and it should be rounded and a little thick, so that it does not bend when compressed on the member under your work, and it should be sharp at the end, and thick at the middle in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason it is necessary that the curved fingers be placed on top of the visible bone; and put it in place once, until it comes back into its proper position, and be equal to each other. And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the tip of the bone, so that the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot put the bone back in place as we have said, then cut it off with an instrument suitable for this, or a saw or knife, to your power; and take out from the bone what is remaining of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is in place and the patient feels great pain afterward, you should know that it is not in its natural position. So, do what it takes to get it into its proper position, then soak a cloth in black vinegar and put it on the wound properly; and do not put cerote or any other ointment with oil on the wound, lest it bring about purulence and corruption. Then administer stitches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut off the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times this has been done by foolish doctors, and they have brought about death or corruption on the patient once. And the constriction should be softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come of it, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then do not put stitches on it; but wrap around it, instead of stitches, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two that there is pus forming at the wound, then take out everything that you had put on it in vinegar, and put on healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacial ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bound in such a way that the lower part bends slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal but instead turns into a swelling, know that it has small bones, so you should sew the wound with thread, and remove all these loose pieces of bone that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or some manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bones of the shin or thigh, and other similar ones from the large limbs, do not pull them out, for many times the wound comes back, but leave it alone until it rots; perhaps it will fall out within twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the blisters that come on the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across this after the healing of the break, especially when it's near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps it cannot make its natural movements.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the blister is fresh: if the administrator uses purgative medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with purgative wine or with almond oil or with vinegar; and put them on the new blister in poultices, and apply pressure well, and do not remove it for one day; and then release it, and start another, as long as the nodules are removed; or you strain against a well-made piece of cloth, because the properties of the cloth are such that they remove all swellings on the members; and if the nodule has already become hardened like a stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so scrape off the superfluous parts above, or take it to a barber, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	from the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone break is restored, and the limb remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one of them is that it was tied too tightly, and not tightened as needed; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment to the member could not come; or due to a multitude of swellings; or because of excessive movements, not in its right time; or because it has too little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make food for the sick person, and make their body tender, until there is a multiplication of blood in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and removes excess fluid, as often as water can, until the nourishment comes to the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	from the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, though it doesn't lose its natural function: don't believe the fools who say that you should break the whole limb again, and many foolish healers have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great harm, and possibly death. However, if the nodules and the twisting are fresh, it is necessary to remove them with hot water or mild herbs, such as leaves of marjoram, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as well-made dyaquilon, and take the milky sap of marjoram, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take plump figs, and grind them with henbane seeds, and similar medicines that soften the inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at no time is the nodule removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. And administer movement to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, so that it must cover just up to the bone, slightly lightly with a sharp incisor; and apply cauterization and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by a joint moving out of its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to anyone, if now it needs to be returned to its original position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joint swells, and by chance if it is put back in place with pain; therefore it does not need to be moved until it has ceased swelling: many times it causes pain and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this happens, it makes the patient heal, then leaves them until the swelling has ceased; then heats the member with hot water and oil, then rinses it lightly, and cures each member as the treatment comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head up to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Whatever happens when the jawbones are dislocated inwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: or they are a little pulled out of their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor close its mouth, and encircle its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it heals in a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and finished, you must rinse it immediately, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the servants put a cloth soaked with hot water on the patient's head, and pour vinegar from a small pot of one hand into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands are outside to put it equally; and command the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the servants place the cloth equally on both sides, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it's difficult to return, even if it's the two jawbones together, then heat them with hot water and oil, until they are rinsed lightly; nor delay in returning, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally and the patient's mouth closes well without any difficulty, then put wet cloths on the affected area in a folded cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie them lightly with soft threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and his dogs (cheekbones) are lying between two cushions, so that he doesn't move them to the right or left, nor does he strain himself to chew, but rather takes light food, until the pains are removed and the jawbones are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then take food lightly as he wishes, and do not work hard to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not turned back to their positions, then fever and sharp stomachaches come, and perhaps intestinal purging, and perhaps vomiting of clean bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a death sentence; and many times the person who has this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the elbow
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The elbow cannot be straightened from the inside towards the shoulder, and it is dislocated only once to the outside, and then one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back and stretches out his arms; then he presses the dislocated joint firmly against your palm, and it will come back into place; then put on the poultice and bandage, and tighten it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the sprain which is next to the elbow cannot be straightened; if it does not, and if it becomes dislocated even once, then it will return to its place, as we have said; then put on the poultice and bandage, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly the sprain of the shoulder can be returned to its place when it is dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
