Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: first, it dislocates from the back part of the blade down; and second, it dislocates from the front part of the chest; and by chance it dislocates upwards, which occurs rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and often it dislocates downward towards the blade, just like those who have little flesh, because it jumps out quickly; to those who have enough flesh, it jumps out with pain, and returns with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a blow or a crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot tumor, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you should examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and once you have confirmed the diagnosis, begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is clear when the dislocation is downward towards the blade, and you will notice a clear difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest diversity between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find on the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the blade at the tip of the shoulder, also just like an owl's head; and the sick person cannot bring their hand to their neck, nor move any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly at the tip of the shoulder.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not to be reduced, when it is new, or if the patient is young.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician lifts the hand of the patient up high, then puts his thumbs under the blade, and lifts the joint with force upwards to its place; and the physician lifts the hand and stretches it up, then places it down; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come back as we said in the time of one day, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the physician should apply soothing and calming remedies, such as a decoction of alecost, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and have them administered.

The joint of the thigh is swollen in four parts: inside and outside, and in front and back; and more severely inside than outside, and swelling in front and back. It seems like a description of the specific symptoms and characteristics of a hip dislocation.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it's longer, and the sick knee joint opens more than the healthy one, and the sick person can't bend their knee joint to fold it. It seems like a description of a clear indication or symptom of a hip dislocation, where the affected limb appears to be out of place or distorted in some way.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it's the spot that is near the inflamed swelling that appears hot, because the veins of the leg come there. It seems like a description of a specific area where the affected limb is swollen and warm to the touch, possibly due to increased blood flow or inflammation in the veins.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes from the outside is that this accident is contrary to those in front. It seems like a description of a type of hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned opposite to its normal position, possibly with the femur head pointing outwards rather than inwards.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that which happens in front are that the leg is bent well according to its completion; however, it cannot bend its knee joint without pain, and if you want to make it walk, it can't move forward, and holds its urine, and swells up the groin, and when it walks, it passes over the heel. It seems like a description of symptoms associated with a hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned in an abnormal way, causing pain and difficulty walking or moving the knee joint.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which happens behind are that it cannot extend its knee joint, nor bend it, and the affected leg is more bent than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the same level as the sides. It seems like a description of symptoms associated with a hip dislocation where the affected limb is positioned in an abnormal way, causing stiffness and softening of the groin area.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you treat it if the dislocation is ancient and has remained in its position, without any cure; and do not have any presumption about it. It seems like a warning to be cautious when treating hip dislocations, especially those that have been present for a long time, as they may be more difficult or impossible to cure.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that where the dislocation is fresh and it's of three types of dislocation, hasten to turn the joint back into place, and make it straight inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for any other treatment. It seems like a description of an emergency procedure to correct a fresh hip dislocation by manually manipulating the joint back into its proper position, with the hope that it will heal on its own without further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it doesn't return in this way, then it is necessary that you summon a strong servant and have him hold the leg firmly with both hands, or with one string that is tied over the knee. It seems like a description of a technique to immobilize the affected limb while trying to reduce the dislocation by applying external pressure or support.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another servant stretches their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the patient's armpits, then they tighten a thin string over the thigh; and another servant ties the end of the string. It seems like a description of a system of manual manipulation and external support to help reduce the dislocation, with multiple people working together to hold the affected limb in place while applying gentle but firm pressure.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch up and down together all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground for one moment, and remains suspended. It seems like a dramatic and intense procedure to reduce the dislocation by lifting the affected limb out of its abnormal position and holding it in place long enough to allow the joint to settle back into its proper alignment.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for all three types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned to its proper place, as we have said, then it's good. It seems like a confirmation that this technique can be used effectively for different types of hip dislocations, and that a successful outcome is desirable.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, then it's necessary to apply a remedy to its appearance. If the dislocation is in the direction of the back, then you should place a bandage on the healthy side of the patient, then tie the string over the root of the thigh, and the part that is underneath the groin; then stretch the string up towards the groin and towards the femoral region. It seems like a description of a technique to apply external support and pressure to help reduce the dislocation by tying a bandage or string around the affected area in a specific way.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another servant's arms and wrap them around the thick part of the patient's sick thigh, and stretch it out to the outside firmly: if it will return to its proper place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others. It seems like a description of a technique where two people work together to apply external pressure to help reduce the dislocation by stretching and holding the affected limb in place.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you can't bind it in this way as we have said, then it's necessary to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong, soft string on both heels and knees, and the sick leg should be stretched out two fingers more than the other. It seems like a description of a technique where the affected limb is immobilized by tying the feet together and stretching the affected leg out further than the healthy one, possibly to help reduce the dislocation or stabilize the joint.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then it should be hung from the head of a beam and be above ground two arms in length; then command one servant to wrap their arms around the patient's thigh and have another servant hang with the patient, who wraps firmly around the thigh, for the joint returns now hastily. It seems like a description of a technique where the affected limb is suspended from a beam and manipulated by servants who apply pressure or support to help reduce the dislocation.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the outside, have the patient lie down as we have said in the case of gibbosity, and tie a string around the sick leg properly, and also around the buttocks. It seems like a description of a technique to immobilize the affected limb by tying a string around it, possibly to help reduce the dislocation or stabilize the joint.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two twigs, one at the head and the other near the feet, then stick the twig between the patient's thighs in the middle of their form. It seems like a description of a technique where wooden supports or splints are placed alongside the patient's body to provide additional support or stability, possibly to help reduce the dislocation or immobilize the affected limb.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have dampened cloths planted all around so that the patient doesn't bleed, then have each servant stretch out towards them, and the person who knows how to do it should place their hand next to the dislocation. It seems like a description of a technique where multiple people work together to support and stabilize the affected limb, while also taking steps to prevent bleeding or injury during the procedure.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns to its place, then that's good. If not, have the patient lie on the table and press in the same way as we have said for gibbosity, and have the patient lie on their healthy side. It seems like a description of a technique to continue trying to reduce the dislocation by applying pressure or support using the "gibbosity" method, possibly with some modifications to accommodate the specific situation.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it's necessary to stretch the sick leg hastily and according to what I've said; and have the person who knows how to do it put their hand on top of the patient's affected groin area, then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the knee. It seems like a description of a technique where pressure is applied to try to reduce the dislocation, possibly by using both hands to manipulate the affected limb in a specific way.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the outside, it's not necessary to extend the sick leg downwards or lift it up off the ground, but rather that it should be in a similar state as if the thigh were dislocated to the outside, as we have said about lying on two thighs. It seems like a description of a technique where the affected limb is positioned in such a way that it's not extended or elevated, but rather held in a neutral position, possibly to help stabilize the joint and prevent further injury.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And it should be on his face, and the thread stretched as we have said before, and you must press on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be in place when the patient stretches out their legs and they are equal; then tie up the thighs, apply the poultice, and strain from a cloth, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and let it rest 3 days or 4, then dislocate and put the poultice on top; and if you see they are equal, add the strain as before, and leave it for 3 days; then dislocate, and let it go slowly, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The kneecap is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if it does not straighten out at their knee, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you have the patient sit up straight, and stretch out their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take hold of their kneecap with your palms and draw it between your two fists, then bend the two sides of the kneecap firmly; and another attendant stretches out their foot until the kneecap returns to its place, and the signs are that they straighten out their leg lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the poultice on top, and make them straighten out their leg at the knee, and tie it all together tightly for 3 days or 4, then loosen; and do not bother to move the patient until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the member is not yet well, have an attendant stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle swells, and it bends forward towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return to normal position is slight, and the leg should be stretched out lightly by hand when it is only sprained.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, it is advisable that you have the patient sit up straight, and another attendant grasp the leg just above the ankle, from behind.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot firmly upwards.
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns to its normal position, it is well; but if not, start again with the task, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return to its normal position, have the patient sit on their back on the ground, and insert a firm pillow or bolster between their thighs, and tie a cloth around it so that it does not injure the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have another attendant take hold of the thigh, and another attendant stretch out the foot to their hands or on a cord, so that they tie it above the ankle.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch out each attendant equally, and the pillow(s) should be placed between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place while it is being stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the patient put their hands equally on either side of the dislocation, and another attendant grasp the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return to its proper place.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is back in its proper place, then apply the poultice and compress on top, and bind the leg firmly to the ankle, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandages are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then let it be for 2 days or 3, and if the bandages loosen, apply the compress again; then on the third day or the fourth, unbind and keep the patient from moving for 4 days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he moves before the set time is up, it's not certain that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the heel, it is advisable that you treat it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is sound.
des dois	of the toes
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the toes are dislocated, they should be gently stretched without force, and it is a slight thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the toe, it is advisable that you have the patient sit on a plain bench or table with their feet straight out, and place your foot so that it presses against the joint, then press firmly until it returns to its proper position.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is straight and there is no problem, place under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then apply a compress firmly, and let it be for 3 days, then unbind it; and have it rest until it is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not cautious in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, nor too hasty.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use in the beginning gentle and soothing things, and leave the patient to God's care, if you do not see hope of healing.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see a chance for recovery, then clean the wound thoroughly with water, so that the hot abscess comes.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is clean, then administer soothing things to the hot abscess, and care for the wound with drying ointments, as is fitting.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones are shattered, then set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases. (meaning to follow standard procedures for setting broken bones)
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and beware of entering a path of fear, as I have said, for it is worth more to you than your creator, and for the sake of knowing how to heal yourself and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the treatise on surgery.
